[Setting status bits in program control operation instructions (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-in-program-control-operation-instructions-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[Evaluating errors with output parameter RET_VAL](Programming%20basics.md#evaluating-errors-with-output-parameter-ret_val)
  
[STL Basics (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#stl-basics-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[Memory areas (S7-300, S7-400)](Functional%20description%20of%20S7-300-400%20CPUs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%29.md#memory-areas-s7-300-s7-400)

#### CiR: Control CiR process (S7-400)

##### Description

The "Control CiR process" instruction is used to influence the CiR process in the user program as follows:

- Disable CiR process. In this case, the download of a modified configuration from the programming device to the CPU is always rejected. The disable is maintained until you cancel it again with the "Control CiR process" instruction.
- You can disable the CiR process conditionally by specifying a high limit for the CiR synchronization time on the FRZ_TIME parameter. In this case, the download of a modified configuration from the programming device to the CPU is only accepted if the CiR synchronization time calculated in the CPU does not exceed the specified high limit.
- Enable CiR process. The high limit of the CiR synchronization time is set to the default value 1000 ms.
- Determine whether the CiR process is enabled or not. If the CiR process is enabled or conditionally enabled, you will get the current high limit for the CiR synchronization time in the A_FT parameter of the instruction.

> **Note**
>
> During the CiR synchronization period the outputs are frozen and the inputs are not evaluated.

##### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Control CiR process" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| MODE | Input | BYTE | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | Job identifier  Valid values on the MODE parameter are:  - 0: Information function - 1: Enable CiR process - 2: Disable CiR process - 3: Disable CiR conditionally. You specify the high limit of the CiR synchronization time in FRZ_TIME. |
| FRZ_TIME | Input | TIME | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | High limit of the CiR synchronization time in milliseconds.   Permitted range of values: 60 ... 2500 ms (default: 1000 ms)  The FRZ_TIME parameter is only relevant when the value 3 is set on the MODE parameter. |
| RET_VAL | Output | INT | I, Q, M, D, L | Error information  When the MODE parameter is "0", the RET_VAL parameter supplies information on the enabling of the CiR process. |
| A_FT | Output | TIME | I, Q, M, D, L | Currently valid high limit of the CiR synchronization time |

##### RET_VAL parameter

The following table shows the meaning of the values of the RET_VAL parameter:

| Error code* (W#16#...) | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| 0000 | Job executed without error  This error code can be output only if the value "1", "2" or "3" is set on the MODE parameter. |
| 0001 | CiR is enabled.   This error code can be output only if the value "0" is set on the MODE parameter. |
| 0002 | The CiR process is disabled.   This error code can be output only if the value "0" is set on the MODE parameter. |
| 0003 | CiR is disabled conditionally.   This error code can be output only if the value "0" is set on the MODE parameter. |
| 8001 | The CPU is not ready for a CiR operation. You are using an H CPU in an H-system (stand-alone), or you are working with a standard CPU in multicomputing mode. |
| 8002 | The value at the MODE parameter is invalid. |
| 8003 | The value at the FRZ_TIME parameter is invalid. |
| 8xyy | You can find additional information here: [Evaluating errors with output parameter RET_VAL](Programming%20basics.md#evaluating-errors-with-output-parameter-ret_val) |
| *The error codes can be displayed as integer or hexadecimal value in the program editor. You can find information on switching the display formats here: [Switching display formats in the program status](Testing%20the%20user%20program.md#switching-display-formats-in-the-program-status) |  |

##### Example

The "Control CiR process" instruction can be used, for example, to ensure that no CiR process is initiated during periods in which maximum CPU performance is required to control the process.

To use the "Control CiR process" for this, the instruction must be called in the program before the start of the period with increased process activity and executed with the value "2" (disable CiR process) for the MODE parameter. The CiR process is then disabled.

To enable the CiR process again after the completion of the period with increased process activity, call the "Control CiR process" instruction again and execute it with the value "1" for the MODE parameter. Alternatively, you can also set the value 3 on the MODE parameter to disable the CiR process conditionally.

---

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)

## Word logic operations (S7-300, S7-400)

This section contains information on the following topics:

- [DECO: Decode (S7-300, S7-400)](#deco-decode-s7-300-s7-400)
- [ENCO: Encode (S7-300, S7-400)](#enco-encode-s7-300-s7-400)
- [SEL: Select (S7-300, S7-400)](#sel-select-s7-300-s7-400)

### DECO: Decode (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

The instruction "Decode" sets a bit specified by the input value in the output value.

The "Decode" instruction reads the value of the IN parameter and sets the bit in the OUT parameter whose bit position corresponds to the value read. The other bits in the output value are filled with zeroes. When the value at the IN parameter is greater than 31, a modulo-32 operation is executed.

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Decode" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| IN | Input | WORD, INT | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | Position of the bit in the output value which is set |
| OUT | Output | DWORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Output value |

You can select the data type of the IN parameter from the "???" drop-down list.

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| CALL DECO | // The instruction is called.  // Select the required data type from the "???" drop-down list. |
| IN := "Tag_Input" | // Input value that specifies the bit to be set in the output value |
| OUT := "Tag_Output" | // Result |

The following table shows how the instruction functions using specific values:

![Example](images/51492948107_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

The instruction reads bit number "3" from the value of the operand "Tag_Input" and sets the third bit to the value of the operand "Tag_Output".

[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

### ENCO: Encode (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

The instruction "Encode" is used to read the bit number of the least significant set bit in the input value and to output it at the parameter OUT.

The "Encode" instruction selects the least significant bit of the value at the IN parameter and writes this bit number to the operand at the OUT parameter. If the IN parameter has the value DW#16#00000001 or DW#16#00000000, the value "0" is output at the OUT parameter.

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Encode" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| IN | Input | DWORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | Input value |
| OUT | Output | INT | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Output value |

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| CALL ENCO | // The instruction is called. |
| IN := "Tag_Input" | // Input value the least significant bit of which is read. |
| OUT := "Tag_Output" | // Bit number of least significant bit set in the input value |

The following table shows how the instruction functions using specific values:

![Example](images/51493666315_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

The instruction selects the least significant set bit of the variable "Tag_Input" and writes its bit position "3" to the variable "Tag_Output".

[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

### SEL: Select (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

Depending on a switch (input G), you use the "Select" instruction to select one of the inputs, IN0 or IN1, and copies its content to the OUT output. If the G input has signal state "0", the value at the IN0 input is moved. If the G input has the signal state "1", the value of the IN1 input is moved to the OUT output.

The instruction is only executed if the tags of all parameters have the same data type.

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Select" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| G | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Switch |
| IN0 | Input | Bit strings, integers, floating-point numbers, timers, CHAR, TOD, DATE | I, Q, M, D, L, P | First input value |
| IN1 | Input | Bit strings, integers, floating-point numbers, timers, CHAR, TOD, DATE | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Second input value |
| OUT | Output | Bit strings, integers, floating-point numbers, timers, CHAR, TOD, DATE | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Result |

You can select the data type of the parameters IN0, IN1 and OUT from the "???" drop-down list.

> **Note**
>
> **Parameter assignment**
>
> In addition, input parameters (Input), output parameters (Output) and in/out parameters (InOut) of functions must not be connected to the input and output parameters of the instruction. If required, use a temporary tag (Temp) as buffer.

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| CALL SEL | // The instruction is called.  // Select the required data type from the "???" drop-down list. |
| G := "Tag_Input_G" | // Signal state of the switch |
| IN0 := "Tag_Input0" | // First input value |
| IN1 := "Tag_Input1" | // Second input value |
| OUT := "Tag_Output" | // Value of the selected input |

The following table shows how the instruction functions using specific values:

| Parameters | Operand | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| G | Tag_Input_G | 1 |
| IN0 | Tag_Input0 | W#16#0000 |
| IN1 | Tag_Input1 | W#16#FFFF |
| OUT | Tag_Output | W#16#FFFF |

---

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)

### SET: Set bit array (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

You use the "Set bit array" instruction to set the signal state of the bits in a specified area to "1". You use the pointer on the S_BIT parameter to define the starting point of the range. If the pointer points to the memory area of the external I/O, the instruction is not executed. You specify the number of bits to be set in the specified area in the N parameter. When the N parameter has the value "0", calling the instruction has no effect.

The instruction is only executed when the MCR bit is "1". When the MCR bit has the signal state "0", the bits in the specified range are not changed.

> **Note**
>
> **Parameter N**
>
> You can also interconnect an element of a data block at parameter N.

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Set bit array" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| S_BIT | Input | POINTER | I, Q, M, D | Pointer to the first bit of the range whose bits are set.  For area-crossing, indirect register addressing, the pointer must be specified in double-word format. |
| N | Input | INT | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | Number of bits to be set |

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| CALL SET | // The "Set bit array" instruction is called |
| S_BIT := P#M0.0 | // Pointer to the first bit to be set (M0.0) |
| N := 10 | // Number of bits to be set |

In the example the instruction sets 10 bits in the range from M0.0 to M1.2.

---

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)
  
[Setting status bits (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-s7-300-s7-400)

[Master Control Relay (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#master-control-relay-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[Memory areas (S7-300, S7-400)](Functional%20description%20of%20S7-300-400%20CPUs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%29.md#memory-areas-s7-300-s7-400)

### SETP: Set a bit array in the I/O area (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

The instruction "Set a bit array in the I/O area" sets the bits of an I/O area to the signal state "1". At the same time the corresponding bits in the process image outputs are also set parallel to the I/O bits.

You use the N and SA parameters to define the bit array that will be set. The bits of the array must be located in the part of the I/O area to which a process image is assigned.

If no I/O devices are plugged in for part of the selected bit array, the instruction attempts to set the entire bit array. In this case an error information is output at the RET_VAL parameter.

The I/O area is set byte-by-byte. If the bit array defined via the N and SA parameters does not begin or end at a byte boundary, calling the instruction has the following effect:

- The bits that are in the first and last bytes to be transferred and that do not belong to the defined bit array, get the value of the corresponding bits in the process image output.

  | Symbol | Meaning |
  | --- | --- |
  |  | **Warning** |
  | **Unintended behavior**  The setting of the bits at the value of the relevant bit in the process image output can lead, for example, to lead to unintended reactions such as starting a motor or turning off a cooling system. |  |
- The bits belonging to the defined bit array are set to the signal state "1".

The instruction "Set a bit array in the I/O area" must be called in an MCR area.

Calling the "Set a bit array in the I/O area" instruction has no effect if one of the following conditions applies:

- The N parameter has the value "0".
- The MCR bit has the signal state "0".

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Set a bit array in the I/O area" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| N | Input | INT | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | Number of bits to be set |
| RET_VAL | Output | INT | I, Q, M, D, L | Error information |
| SA | Output | POINTER | P | Pointer to the first bit to be set |

#### RET_VAL parameter

The following table shows the meaning of the values of the RET_VAL parameter:

| Error code* (W#16#...) | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| 0000 | No error |
| 8xyy | You can find additional information here: [Evaluating errors with output parameter RET_VAL](Programming%20basics.md#evaluating-errors-with-output-parameter-ret_val) |
| *The error codes can be displayed as integer or hexadecimal value in the program editor. You can find information on switching the display formats here: [Switching display formats in the program status](Testing%20the%20user%20program.md#switching-display-formats-in-the-program-status) |  |

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| CALL SETP | // The instruction is called. |
| N := 8 | // Number of bits to be set |
| RET_VAL := "Tag_ErrorCode" | // Error information |
| SA := P#10.0 | // Pointer to the first bit to be set (Q10.0) |

In the example the instruction sets 8 bits in the I/O range corresponding to the outputs Q10.0 to Q10.7.

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)
  
[Setting status bits (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[STL Basics (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#stl-basics-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[Memory areas (S7-300, S7-400)](Functional%20description%20of%20S7-300-400%20CPUs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%29.md#memory-areas-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[Master Control Relay (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#master-control-relay-s7-300-s7-400)

### SETI: Set byte array (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

The "Set byte array" instruction sets the signal state of the bits in a specified area of bytes to "1". You define the start point of the array on the S_BYTE. You define the size of the array by specifying the number of bits to be set on the N parameter of the instruction.

> **Note**
>
> The value of the N parameter must be a multiple of the number eight (for example, 8, 16, 24, etc.).

The pointer specified on the S_BYTE parameter must reference the external I/O memory area (P). Since the "P" memory area is accessed as bytes, words, or double words, the pointer of the S_BYTE parameter must point to an operand that corresponds to a byte limit value, i.e., the bit number of the pointer must be "0".

> **Note**
>
> The signal state of the corresponding bits in the process-image output (Q) is reset to "0".

Calling the "Set byte array" instruction has no effect if one of the following conditions applies:

- The pointer on the S_BYTE parameter does not reference the external I/O memory area (P).
- The pointer on the S_BYTE parameter references an operand that is not byte-aligned.
- The value of the N parameter is not a multiple of the number 8.
- The MCR bit has the signal state "0".

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Set byte array" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| S_BYTE | Input | POINTER | P or constant | Points to the first byte of the array whose bits will be set  For area-crossing, indirect register addressing, the pointer must be specified in double-word format. |
| N | Input | INT | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | Size of the array to be set  The array is specified by the number of bits as a multiple of eight (for example 8, 16, 24 etc.). |

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| CALL SETI | // The instruction is called. |
| S_BYTE := P#2.0 | // Pointer to the first byte of the range (P2.0) |
| N := 16 | // Number of bits to be set |

In the example the instruction sets 2 bytes (16 bits) in the range from P2.0 to P3.7 (I/O outputs).

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)
  
[Setting status bits (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-s7-300-s7-400)

### RESET: Reset bit array (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

The "Reset bit array" instruction is used to reset the signal state of the bits in a specified range to "0". You use the pointer on the S_BIT parameter to define the starting point of the range. If the pointer points to the memory area of the external I/O, the instruction is not executed. You specify the number of bits to be reset in the specified range at the N parameter of the instruction. When the N parameter has the value "0", calling the instruction has no effect.

The instruction is only executed when the MCR bit is "1". When the MCR bit has the signal state "0", the bits in the specified range are not changed.

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Reset bit array" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| S_BIT | Input | POINTER | I, Q, M, D | Points to the first bit of the range whose bits will be reset.  For area-crossing, indirect register addressing, the pointer must be specified in double-word format. |
| N | Input | INT | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | Number of bits to be reset. |

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| CALL RESET | // The instruction is called. |
| S_BIT := P#M0.0 | // Pointer to the first bit (M0.0) to be reset |
| N := 10 | // Number of bits which are reset |

In the example the instruction resets 10 bits in the range from M0.0 to M1.2.

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)

### RESETP: Reset a bit array in the I/O area (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

The "Reset a bit array in the I/O area" instruction is used to reset the bits of an I/O area to signal state "0". At the same time the corresponding bits in the process image outputs are also reset parallel to the I/O bits.

You use the N and SA parameters to define the bit array that will be reset. The bits of the array must be located in the part of the I/O area to which a process image is assigned.

The I/O area is reset byte-by-byte. If the bit array defined via the N and SA parameters does not begin or end at a byte boundary, calling the instruction has the following effect:

- The bits that are in the first and last bytes to be transferred and that do not belong to the defined bit array, get the value of the corresponding bits in the process image output.

  | Symbol | Meaning |
  | --- | --- |
  |  | **Warning** |
  | **Unintended behavior**  The setting of the bits at the value of the relevant bit in the process image output can lead, for example, to lead to unintended reactions such as starting a motor or turning off a cooling system. |  |
- The bits belonging to the defined bit array are reset to the signal state "0".

The instruction "Reset a bit array in the I/O area" must be called in an MCR range.

Calling the "Reset a bit array in the I/O area" instruction has no effect if one of the following conditions applies:

- The N parameter has the value "0".
- The MCR bit has the signal state "0".

| --- | --- |

The following example shows how the instruction works:

The "Reset byte array" instruction is used to reset the signal state of the bits in a specified range of bytes to "0". ### REPL_VAL: Enter substitute value (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

Use the "Enter substitute value" instruction to enter a substitute value in accumulator 1 (ACCU 1) from a synchronous error organization block of the program level causing the error.

> **Note**
>
> You can only call the "Enter substitute value" instruction in a synchronous error organization block (OB 121, OB 122).

Use the "Enter substitute value" instruction when you can no longer read any value from a module. The OB 122 is started after each access to this module. By calling the "Enter substitute value" instruction you can have the substitute value loaded in accumulator 1 of the interrupted program level. The program execution is then continued with this substitute value. The information needed for selecting the substitute value (for example, the block in which the error occurred or the address affected) is located in the local tags of OB 122.

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Enter substitute value" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| VAL | Input | DWORD | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | Substitute value |
| RET_VAL | Output | INT | I, Q, M, D, L | Error information |

#### Parameter RET_VAL

The following table shows the meaning of the values of the RET_VAL parameter:

| Error code*  (W#16#...) | Description |
| --- | --- |
| 0000 | No error |
| 8080 | The instruction was not called from a synchronous error OB. |
| 8xyy | You can find additional information here: [Evaluating errors with output parameter RET_VAL](Programming%20basics.md#evaluating-errors-with-output-parameter-ret_val) |
| *The error codes can be displayed as integer or hexadecimal value in the program editor. You can find information on switching the display formats here: [Switching display formats in the program status](Testing%20the%20user%20program.md#switching-display-formats-in-the-program-status) |  |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)
  
[Setting status bits (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[STL Basics (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#stl-basics-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[Memory areas (S7-300, S7-400)](Functional%20description%20of%20S7-300-400%20CPUs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%29.md#memory-areas-s7-300-s7-400)

### DRUM: Implement sequencer (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

You use the "Implement sequencer" instruction to assign the programmed output bits (OUT1 to OUT16) and the output word (OUT_WORD) with the programmed values of the OUT_VAL parameter of the relevant step. The specific step must thereby satisfy the conditions of the programmed enable mask on the S_MASK parameter while the instruction remains at this step. The instruction advances to the next step if the event for the step is true and the programmed time for the current step elapses, or if the value at the JOG parameter changes from "0" to "1". The instruction is reset when the signal state of the RESET parameter changes to "1". The current step is hereby equated to the preset step (DSP).

The amount of time spent on a step is determined by the product of the preset timebase (DTBP) and the preset counter value (S_PRESET) for each step. At the start of a new step, this calculated value is loaded into the DCC parameter, which contains the time remaining for the current step. If, for example the value at the DTBP parameter is "2" and the preset value for the first step is "100" (100 ms), the DCC parameter has the value "200" (200 ms).

A step can be programmed with a timer value, an event, or both. Steps that have an event bit and the timer value "0" advance to the next step as soon as the signal state of the event bit is "1". Steps that are programmed only with a timer value start the time immediately. Steps that are programmed with an event bit and a time value greater than "0" start the time when the signal state of the event bit is "1". The event bits are initialized with a signal state of "1".

When the sequencer is on the last programmed step (LST_STEP) and the time for this step has expired, the signal state on the Q parameter is set to "1"; otherwise it is set to "0". When the Q parameter is set, the instruction remains on the step until it is reset.

In the configurable mask (S_MASK) you can select the individual bits in the output word (OUT_WORD) and set or reset the output bits (OUT1 to OUT16) by means of the output values (OUT_VAL). When a bit of the configurable mask has a signal state of "1", the OUT_VAL value sets/resets the corresponding bit. If the signal state of a bit of the configurable mask is "0", the corresponding bit is left unchanged. All the bits of the configurable mask for all 16 steps are initialized with a signal state of "1".

The output bit on the OUT1 parameter corresponds to the least significant bit of the output word (OUT_WORD). The output bit on the OUT16 parameter corresponds to the most significant bit of the output word (OUT_WORD).

When you insert the instruction in the program, the "Call options" dialog opens in which you can specify whether the block parameters will be stored in a separate data block (single instance) or as a local tag (multiple instance) in the block interface. If you create a separate data block, you will find it in the project tree in the "Program resources" folder under "Program blocks &gt; System blocks". For additional information on this topic, refer to "See also".

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Implement sequencer" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| RESET | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | A signal state of "1" indicates a reset condition |
| JOG | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | When the signal state changes from "0" to "1", the instruction advances to the next step. |
| DRUM_EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | The signal state "1" allows the sequencer to advance based on the event and time criteria. |
| LST_STEP | Input | BYTE | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | Number of the last programmed step. |
| EVENT(i),  1&lt;= i &lt;=16 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Event bit (i);  Initial signal state is "1". |
| OUT(j),  1 ≤ j ≤ 16 | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Output bit (j) |
| Q | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | The signal state "1" indicates that the time for the last step has elapsed. |
| OUT_WORD | Output | WORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Word address to which the sequencer writes the output values. |
| ERR_CODE | Output | WORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Error information |
| JOG_HIS | Static | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | JOG parameter history bit |
| EOD | Static | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | The signal state "1" indicates that the time for the last step has elapsed. |
| DSP | Static | BYTE | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Preset first step of the sequencer (1 to 16) |
| DSC | Static | BYTE | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Current step of the sequencer |
| DCC | Static | DWORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Remaining processing time for the current step |
| DTBP | Static | WORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Preset timebase of the sequencer |
| PrevTime | Static | TIME | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | System time of the previous call |
| S_PRESET | Static | ARRAY[1..16] of WORD | I, Q, M, D, L | Preset counter value for each step [1 to 16] where one clock pulse = 1 ms. |
| OUT_VAL | Static | ARRAY[1..16, 0..15] of BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Output values for each step [1 to 16, 0 to 15]. |
| S_MASK | Static | ARRAY[1..16, 0..15] of BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Configurable mask for each step [1 to 16, 0 to 15]. Initial signal states are "1". |

#### ERR_CODE parameter

The following table shows the meaning of the values of the ERR_CODE parameter:

| ERR_CODE* | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| W#16#0000 | No error |
| W#16#000B | The value at the LST_STEP parameter is less than 1 or greater than 16. |
| W#16#000C | The value at the DSC parameter is less than 1 or greater than the value of the LST_STEP parameter. |
| W#16#000D | The value at the DSP parameter is less than 1 or greater than the value of the LST_STEP parameter. |
| *The error codes can be displayed as integer or hexadecimal value in the program editor. You can find information on switching the display formats here: [Switching display formats in the program status](Testing%20the%20user%20program.md#switching-display-formats-in-the-program-status) |  |

#### Example

In the following example the instruction advances from step 1 to step 2. The output bits (OUT1 to OUT16) and the output word (OUT_WORD) are set according to the mask configured for step 2 and the values of the OUT_VAL parameter.

> **Note**
>
> You can initialize static parameters in the data block.

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| CALL DRUM, "DRUM_DB" | // The instruction is called and the instance data block "DRUM_DB" is created. |
| RESET := "Tag_Reset" | // Reset input |
| JOG := "Tag_Input_Jog" | // On a rising edge, the instruction advances to the next step |
| DRUM_EN := "Tag_Input_DrumEN" | // The signal state "1" allows the sequencer to advance based on the event and time criteria. |
| LST_STEP := "Tag_Number_LastStep" | // Number of the last programmed step |
| EVENT1 := "MyTag_Event_1" | // Event bit 1 |
| EVENT2 := "MyTag_Event_2" | // Event bit 2 |
| EVENT3 := "MyTag_Event_3" | // Event bit 3 |
| EVENT4 := "MyTag_Event_4" | // Event bit 4 |

| ERR_CODE := "Tag_ErrorCode" | // Error information |

### DRUM_X: Implement sequencer (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

You use the "Implement sequencer" instruction to implement a sequencer with a maximum of 16 steps. You specify the number of the first step on the DSP parameter. You specify the number of the last step on the LST_STEP parameter.

During each step, all 16 output bits OUT0 to OUT15 and the output parameter OUT_WORD (in which the output bits are collected together) are written. An output bit is assigned either the corresponding bit of the OUT_VAL array that you specified or the output bit of the preceding step. The value assigned depends on the value of the mask bit on the S_MASK parameter.

> **Note**
>
> The default of the mask bits is 0. If you want to change the current setting of one or more mask bits, make this change in the instance data block.

The "Implement sequencer" instruction advances to the next step when there is a rising signal edge on the JOG parameter. If the instruction is already in the last step, the Q and EOD tags are set when the JOG parameter has a positive signal edge. In this case the DCC parameter is set to the value "0". The instruction remains in the last step until the RESET parameter is set to the value "1".

You can also assign parameters so that switching to the next step is time dependent. To do this, the DRUM_EN parameter has to be set to the value "1". The transition to the next step is made when the event bit (EVENTi) belonging to the current step is set and the time specified for the current step has expired. The time for a step is the product of the (DTBP) time base and the time factor valid for the current step (S_PRESET).

> **Note**
>
> The execution time (DCC) remaining in the current step is reduced only when the corresponding event bit (EVENTi) is set.

When you insert the instruction in the program, the "Call options" dialog opens in which you can specify whether the block parameters will be stored in a separate data block (single instance) or as a local tag (multiple instance) in the block interface. If you create a separate data block, you will find it in the project tree in the "Program resources" folder under "Program blocks &gt; System blocks". For additional information on this topic, refer to "See also".

If the value "1" is set in the RESET parameter when the instruction is called, the sequencer goes to the step whose number is specified in the DSP parameter.

A step can be programmed with a timer value, an event, or both. Steps that have an event bit and the timer value "0" advance to the next step as soon as the signal state of the event bit is "1". Steps that are programmed only with a timer value start the time immediately. Steps that are programmed with an event bit and a time value greater than "0" start the time when the signal state of the event bit is "1".

You can also move the next step at any time via the value at the JOG parameter.

When the instruction is called for the first time, you must set the value "1" on the RESET parameter.

When the sequencer is in the last step and the execution time specified for this step has expired, the parameters Q and EOD are set. The instruction remains in the last step until the RESET parameter changes to the value "1".

The instruction is executed only in the STARTUP and RUN modes.

The operating system resets the "Implement sequencer" instruction during a cold restart. During a warm restart, the instruction is not reset. If you want the "Implement sequencer" instruction to be initialized after a warm restart, you must call the instruction in OB 100 with the value "1" in the RESET parameter.

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Implement sequencer" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| RESET | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | The signal state "1" resets the sequencer. When the instruction is called for the first time, the RESET parameter must be set to "1". |
| JOG | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | A rising edge (compared to the last call) switches the sequencer to the next step if it is not yet in the last step. The next step is enabled depending on the value you assigned to the DRUM_EN parameter. |
| DRUM_EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Control parameter that specifies whether time-dependent switching to the next step is possible. If the value is "1" a time-dependent switching to the next step is possible. |
| LST_STEP | Input | BYTE | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | Number of the last step   Values from 1 to 16 are permitted. |
| EVENT(i),  1 ≤ i ≤ 16 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Event bit (i) (belongs to step i) |
| OUTj,  0 ≤ j ≤ 15 | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Output bit (j)  (identical with bit no. j of OUT_WORD) |
| Q | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Status parameter that indicates whether the specified execution time of the last step has expired. |
| OUT_WORD | Output | WORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Output bits collected together in a tag |
| ERR_CODE | Output | WORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Error information |
| JOG_HIS | Static | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Not relevant to user (input parameter JOG of the preceding call) |
| EOD | Static | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Identical with output parameter Q |
| DSP | Static | BYTE | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | Number of the first step  Values from 1 to 16 are permitted. |
| DSC | Static | BYTE | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | Number of the current step |
| DCC | Static | DWORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P | The execution time still remaining in the current step in milliseconds (ms) (only relevant if DRUM_EN = 1 and the corresponding event bit = 1) |
| DTBP | Static | WORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | The time base valid for all steps in milliseconds (ms) |
| PREV_TIME | Static | DWORD | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | (Not relevant for the user: system time of the previous call) |
| S_PRESET | Static | ARRAY of WORD | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | One-dimensional array with the time factors for each step.  Recommended selection of the indices: [1 to 16]  In this case, S_PRESET [x] has the time factor of step x. |
| OUT_VAL | Static | ARRAY of BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Two-dimensional array with the values to be output in each step if they have not been masked out using S_MASK.  Recommended selection of the indices: [1 to 16, 0 to 15] In this case, OUT_VAL [x, y] has the value assigned to the output bit OUTy in step x. |
| S_MASK | Static | ARRAY of BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Two-dimensional array with the mask bits for each step.  Recommended selection of the indices: [1 to 16, 0 to 15] In this case, S_MASK [x, y] contains the mask bit for the "y"the value to be output in step x.  Meaning of the mask bits:  - 0: The corresponding value of the previous step is assigned to the relevant output bit. - 1: The corresponding value from OUT_VAL is assigned to the relevant output bit. |

For additional information on valid data types, refer to "See also".

#### ERR_CODE parameter

The following table shows the meaning of the values of the ERR_CODE parameter:

| ERR_CODE* (W#16#...) | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| 0000 | No error |
| 8081 | Invalid value at parameter LST_STEP |
| 8082 | Invalid value on parameter DSC |
| 8083 | Invalid value on parameter DSP |
| 8084 | The product DCC = DTBP * S_PRESET[DSC] exceeds the value 2**31-1 (approximately 24.86 days). |
| *The error codes can be displayed as integer or hexadecimal value in the program editor. You can find information on switching the display formats here: [Switching display formats in the program status](Testing%20the%20user%20program.md#switching-display-formats-in-the-program-status) |  |

#### Example

In the following example the instruction advances from step 1 to step 2. The output bits (OUT0 to OUT15) and the output word (OUT_WORD) are set according to the mask configured for step 2 and the values of the OUT_VAL parameter.

> **Note**
>
> You can initialize static parameters in the data block.

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| CALL DRUM_X, "DRUM_X_DB" | // The instruction is called and the instance data block "DRUM_DB" is created. |
| RESET := "Tag_Reset" | // Reset input |

| LST_STEP := "Tag_Number_LastStep" | // Number of the last programmed step |
| EVENT1 := "MyTag_Event_1" | // Event bit 1 |
| EVENT2 := "MyTag_Event_2" | // Event bit 2 |
| EVENT3 := "MyTag_Event_3" | // Event bit 3 |
| EVENT4 := "MyTag_Event_4" | // Event bit 4 |

| OUT1 | MyTag_Output_1 | M4.1 | TRUE |
| OUT2 | MyTag_Output_2 | M4.2 | TRUE |
| OUT3 | MyTag_Output_3 | M4.3 | TRUE |
| OUT4 | MyTag_Output_4 | M4.4 | TRUE |
| OUT5 | MyTag_Output_5 | M4.5 | TRUE |
| OUT6 | MyTag_Output_6 | M4.6 | TRUE |
| OUT7 | MyTag_Output_7 | M4.7 | TRUE |
| OUT8 | MyTag_Output_8 | M5.0 | TRUE |
| OUT9 | MyTag_Output_9 | M5.1 | TRUE |
| OUT10 | MyTag_Output_10 | M5.2 | TRUE |
| OUT11 | MyTag_Output_11 | M5.3 | TRUE |
| OUT12 | MyTag_Output_12 | M5.4 | TRUE |
| OUT13 | MyTag_Output_13 | M5.5 | TRUE |
| OUT14 | MyTag_Output_14 | M5.6 | TRUE |
| OUT15 | MyTag_Output_15 | M5.7 | TRUE |

#### After processing

The following values are written to the output parameters after the instruction has been executed:

| Parameters | Operand | Address | Value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| OUT0 | MyTag_Output_0 | M4.0 | TRUE |
| OUT1 | MyTag_Output_1 | M4.1 | FALSE |
| OUT2 | MyTag_Output_2 | M4.2 | FALSE |
| OUT3 | MyTag_Output_3 | M4.3 | FALSE |
| OUT4 | MyTag_Output_4 | M4.4 | FALSE |
| OUT5 | MyTag_Output_5 | M4.5 | TRUE |
| OUT6 | MyTag_Output_6 | M4.6 | FALSE |
| OUT7 | MyTag_Output_7 | M4.7 | FALSE |
| OUT8 | MyTag_Output_8 | M5.0 | TRUE |
| OUT9 | MyTag_Output_9 | M5.1 | TRUE |
| OUT10 | MyTag_Output_10 | M5.2 | FALSE |
| OUT11 | MyTag_Output_11 | M5.3 | FALSE |
| OUT12 | MyTag_Output_12 | M5.4 | FALSE |
| OUT13 | MyTag_Output_13 | M5.5 | FALSE |
| OUT14 | MyTag_Output_14 | M5.6 | TRUE |
| OUT15 | MyTag_Output_15 | M5.7 | FALSE |
| Q | Tag_Output_Q | M6.0 | FALSE |
| OUTWORD | Tag_OutputWord | MW8 | W#16#4321 |
| ERR_CODE | Tag_ErrorCode | MW10 | W#16#0000 |

The following values are saved in the "DRUM_X_DB" instance data block of the instruction:

| Parameters | Address | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| JOG_HIS | DBX12.0 | FALSE |
| EOD | DBX12.1 | FALSE |
| DSC | DBB14 | W#16#0002 |
| DCC | DBD16 | DW#16#000000C8 |

### DCAT: Discrete control-timer alarm (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

You can use the "Discrete control-timer alarm" to count the time from the point at which the CMD parameter issues the command to open or close. The time is accumulated until the preset time (PT) is exceeded or the information is received that the device was opened or closed (O_FB or C_FB) within the specified time. If the preset time is exceeded before the information on the opening or closing of the device is received, the corresponding alarm is activated. If the signal state of the command input changes before the preset time, the time is restarted.

When you insert the instruction in the program, the "Call options" dialog opens in which you can specify whether the block parameters will be stored in a separate data block (single instance) or as a local tag (multiple instance) in the block interface. If you create a separate data block, you will find it in the project tree in the "Program resources" folder under "Program blocks &gt; System blocks". For additional information on this topic, refer to "See also".

The "Discrete control-timer alarm" instruction has the following effects on the input conditions:

- When the signal state of the CMD parameter changes from "0" to "1", the signal states of the parameters Q, CMD_HIS, ET, OA and CA are influenced as follows:

  - The parameters Q and CMD_HIS are set to "1".
  - The parameters ET, OA and CA are reset to "0".
- When the signal state on the parameter CMD changes from "1" to "0", the parameters Q, ET, OA, CA and CMD_HIS are reset to "0".
- When the signal state of the CMD and CMD_HIS parameters is "1" and the parameter O_FB is set to "0", the time difference (ms) since the last execution of the instruction is added to the value at the parameter ET. If the value of the ET parameter exceeds the value of the PT parameter, the signal state at the OA parameter is set to "1". If the value of the ET parameter does not exceed the value of the PT parameter, the signal state of the OA parameter is reset to "0". The value at the parameter CMD_HIS is reset to the value of the parameter CMD.
- When the signal state of the parameters CMD, CMD_HIS and O_FB are set to "1" and the parameter C_FB has the value "0", the signal state of the parameter OA is set to "0". The value of the ET parameter is set to the value of the PT parameter. If the signal state of the parameter O_FB changes to "0", the alarm is set the next time the instruction is executed. The value of the CMD_HIS parameter is set to the value of the CMD parameter.
- If the parameters CMD, CMD_HIS and C_FB have the value "0", the time difference (ms) since the last execution of the instruction is added to the value of the parameter ET. If the value of the ET parameter exceeds the value of the PT parameter, the signal state of the parameter CA is reset to "1". If the value at the parameter PT is not exceeded, the parameter CA has the signal state "0". The value of the CMD_HIS parameter is set to the value of the CMD parameter.
- If the parameters CMD, CMD_HIS and O_FB have the signal state "0" and the parameter C_FB is set to "1", the parameter CA is set to "0". The value of the ET parameter is set to the value of the PT parameter. If the signal state of the C_FB parameter changes to "0", the alarm is set the next time the instruction is executed. The value of the CMD_HIS parameter is set to the value of the CMD parameter.
- If the parameters O_FB and C_FB simultaneously have the signal state "1", the signal states of both alarm outputs are set to "1".

The "Discrete control-timer alarm" instruction has no error information.

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Discrete control-timer alarm" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| CMD | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | A signal state of "0" indicates a "close" command.  A signal state of "1" indicates an "open" command. |
| O_FB | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Feedback input when opening |
| C_FB | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Feedback input when closing |
| Q | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Shows the status of the parameter CMD |
| OA | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Alarm output when opening |
| CA | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Alarm output when closing |
| ET | Static | DINT | I, Q, M, D, L | Currently elapsed time, where one count = 1 ms. |
| PT | Static | DINT | I, Q, M, D, L | Preset timer value, where one clock pulse = 1 ms. |
| PREV_TIME | Static | DWORD | I, Q, M, D, L | Previous system time |
| CMD_HIS | Static | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | CMD history bit |

#### Example

In the following example the parameter CMD changes from "0" to "1". After the execution of the instruction the parameter Q is set to "1" and the two alarm outputs OA and CA have the signal state "0". The CMD_HIS parameter of the instance data block is set to the signal state "1" and the ET parameter is reset to "0".

> **Note**
>
> You can initialize static parameters in the data block.

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| CALL DCAT, "DCAT_DB" | // The instruction is called and the instance data block "DCAT_DB" is created. |
| CMD := "Tag_Input_CMD" | // Opening or closing of device |
| O_FB := "Tag_Input_O_FB" | // Feedback when opening |
| C_FB := "Tag_Input_C_FB" | // Feedback when closing |
| Q := "Tag_Output_Q" | // Shows the status of the parameter CMD |
| OA := "Tag_Output_OA" | // Alarm output when opening |
| CA := "Tag_Output_CA" | // Alarm output when closing |

The following tables show how the instruction works using specific values.

#### Before processing

In this example, the following values are used for the input and output parameters:

| Parameters | Operand | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| CMD | Tag_Input_CMD | TRUE |
| O_FB | Tag_Input_O_FB | FALSE |
| C_FB | Tag_Input_C_FB | FALSE |
| Q | Tag_Output_Q | FALSE |
| OA | Tag_Output_OA | FALSE |
| CA | Tag_Output_CA | FALSE |

The following values are saved in the instance data block "DCAT_DB" of the instruction:

| Parameters | Address | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| ET | DBD4 | L#12 |
| PT | DBD8 | L#222 |
| CMD_HIS | DBX16.0 | FALSE |

#### After processing

The following values are written to the output parameters after the instruction has been executed:

| Parameters | Operand | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Q | Tag_Output_Q | TRUE |
| OA | Tag_Output_OA | FALSE |
| CA | Tag_Output_CA | FALSE |

The following values are saved in the instance data block "DCAT_DB" of the instruction:

| Parameters | Address | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| ET | DBD4 | L#0 |
| CMD_HIS | DBX16.0 | TRUE |

---

### MCAT: Motor control-timer alarm (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

The "Motor control-timer alarm" instruction is used to accumulate the time from the point at which one of the command inputs (opening or closing) is switched on. The time is accumulated until the preset time is exceeded or the relevant feedback input indicates that the device has executed the requested operation within the specified time. If the preset time is exceeded before the feedback is received, the corresponding alarm is triggered.

When you insert the instruction in the program, the "Call options" dialog opens in which you can specify whether the block parameters will be stored in a separate data block (single instance) or as a local tag (multiple instance) in the block interface. If you create a separate data block, you will find it in the project tree in the "Program resources" folder under "Program blocks &gt; System blocks". For additional information on this topic, refer to "See also".

#### Execution of the "Motor control-timer alarm" instruction

The following table shows the reactions of the "Motor control-timer alarm" instruction to the various input conditions:

| Input parameters |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | Output parameters |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| ET | O_HIS | C_HIS |  | O_CMD | C_CMD | S_CMD | O_FB | C_FB | OO | CO | OA | CA | ET | O_HIS | C_HIS | Q | Status |
| X | 1 | 1 |  | X | X | X | X | X | 0 | 0 | 1 | 1 | PT | 0 | 0 | 0 | Alarm |
| X | X | X |  | X | X | X | 1 | 1 | 0 | 0 | 1 | 1 | PT | 0 | 0 | 0 | Alarm |
| X | X | X |  | X | X | 1 | X | X | 0 | 0 | 0 | 0 | X | 0 | 0 | 1 | Stop |
| X | X | X |  | 1 | 1 | X | X | X | 0 | 0 | 0 | 0 | X | 0 | 0 | 1 | Stop |
| X | 0 | X |  | 1 | 0 | 0 | X | X | 1 | 0 | 0 | 0 | 0 | 1 | 0 | 1 | Start opening |
| &lt;PT | 1 | 0 |  | X | 0 | 0 | 0 | X | 1 | 0 | 0 | 0 | INC | 1 | 0 | 1 | Open |
| X | 1 | 0 |  | X | 0 | 0 | 1 | 0 | 0 | 0 | 0 | 0 | PT | 1 | 0 | 1 | Opened |
| &gt;=PT | 1 | 0 |  | X | 0 | 0 | 0 | X | 0 | 0 | 1 | 0 | PT | 1 | 0 | 0 | Opening alarm |
| X | X | 0 |  | 0 | 1 | 0 | X | X | 0 | 1 | 0 | 0 | 0 | 0 | 1 | 1 | Start closing |
| &lt;PT | 0 | 1 |  | 0 | X | 0 | X | 0 | 0 | 1 | 0 | 0 | INC | 0 | 1 | 1 | Close |
| X | 0 | 1 |  | 0 | X | 0 | 0 | 1 | 0 | 0 | 0 | 0 | PT | 0 | 1 | 1 | Closed |
| &gt;=PT | 0 | 1 |  | 0 | X | 0 | X | 0 | 0 | 0 | 0 | 1 | PT | 0 | 1 | 0 | Closing alarm |
| X | 0 | 0 |  | 0 | 0 | 0 | X | X | 0 | 0 | 0 | 0 | X | 0 | 0 | 1 | Stopped |
| Legend: |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| INC |  |  | Add the time difference (ms) since the last processing of the FB to ET |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| PT |  |  | PT is set to the same value as ET |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| X |  |  | Cannot be used |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| &lt;PT |  |  | ET &lt; PT |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| &gt;=PT |  |  | ET &gt;= PT |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| When the input parameters O_HIS and C_HIS both have the signal state "1", they are immediately set to the signal state "0". In this case, the last row in the table (X) mentioned above is valid. Because it is therefore not possible to check whether the input parameters O_HIS and C_HIS have the signal state "1", the output parameters are set as follows in this case:   OO = FALSE  CO = FALSE  OA = FALSE  CA = FALSE  ET = PT  Q = TRUE |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Motor control-timer alarm" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| O_CMD | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | "Open" command input |
| C_CMD | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | "Close" command input |
| S_CMD | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | "Stop" command input |
| O_FB | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Feedback input when opening |
| C_FB | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Feedback input when closing |
| OO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | "Open" output |
| CO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | "Close" output |
| OA | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Alarm output when opening |
| CA | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Alarm output when closing |
| Q | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | The signal state "0" indicates an error condition |
| ET | Static | DINT | I, Q, M, D, L | Currently elapsed time, where one count = 1 ms |
| PT | Static | DINT | I, Q, M, D, L | Preset timer value, where one clock pulse = 1 ms |
| PREV_TIME | Static | DWORD | I, Q, M, D, L | Previous system time |
| O_HIS | Static | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | "Open" history bit |
| C_HIS | Static | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | "Close" history bit |

For additional information on valid data types, refer to "See also".

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

> **Note**
>
> You can initialize static parameters in the data block.

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| CALL MCAT, "MCAT_DB" | // The instruction is called and the instance data block "MCAT_DB" is created. |

| C_CMD := "Tag_Input_C_CMD" | // "Close" command input |
| S_CMD := "Tag_Input_S_CMD" | // "Stop" command input |
| O_FB := "Tag_Input_O_FB" | // Feedback when opening |
| C_FB := "Tag_Input_C_FB" | // Feedback when closing |
| OO := "Tag_OutputOpen" | // "Open" output |
| CO := "Tag_OutputClosed" | // "Close" output |
| OA := "Tag_Output_OA" | // Alarm output when opening |
| CA := "Tag_Output_CA" | // Alarm output when closing |
| Q := "Tag_Output_Q" | // Error information |

The following tables show how the instruction works using specific values.

| Parameters | Operand | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| O_CMD | Tag_Input_O_CMD | TRUE |
| C_CMD | Tag_Input_C_CMD | FALSE |
| S_CMD | Tag_Input_S_CMD | FALSE |
| O_FB | Tag_Input_O_FB | FALSE |
| C_FB | Tag_Input_C_FB | FALSE |
| OO | Tag_OutputOpen | FALSE |
| CO | Tag_OutputClosed | FALSE |
| OA | Tag_Output_OA | FALSE |
| CA | Tag_Output_CA | FALSE |
| Q | Tag_Output_Q | FALSE |

The following values are saved in the instance data block "MCAT_DB" of the instruction:

| Parameters | Address | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| ET | DBD4 | L#2 |
| PT | DBD8 | L#22 |
| O_HIS | DBX16.0 | TRUE |
| C_HIS | DBX16.1 | FALSE |

#### After processing

The following values are written to the output parameters after the instruction has been executed:

| Parameters | Operand | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| OO | Tag_OutputOpen | TRUE |
| CO | Tag_OutputClosed | FALSE |
| OA | Tag_Output_OA | FALSE |
| CA | Tag_Output_CA | FALSE |
| Q | Tag_Output_Q | TRUE |

The following values are saved in the instance data block "MCAT_DB" of the instruction:

| Parameters | Address | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| ET | DBD4 | L#0 |
| O_HIS | DBX16.0 | TRUE |
| CMD_HIS | DBX16.1 | FALSE |

### IMC: Compare input bits with the bits of a mask (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

You can use the "Compare input bits with the bits of a mask" instruction to compare the signal state of up to 16 programmed input bits (IN_BIT0 to IN_BIT15) with the corresponding bits of a mask. Up to 16 steps with masks can be programmed. The value of the IN_BIT0 parameter is compared with the value of the mask CMP_VAL[x,0], with "x" indicating the step number. In the CMP_STEP parameter, you specify the step number of the mask that is used for the comparison. All programmed values are compared in the same manner. Unprogrammed input bits or unprogrammed bits of the mask have a default signal state FALSE.

If a match is found in the comparison, the signal state of the OUT parameter is set to "1". Otherwise the OUT parameter is set to "0".

If the value of the CMP_STEP parameter is greater than 15, the instruction is not executed. An error message is output at the ERR_CODE parameter.

When you insert the instruction in the program, the "Call options" dialog opens in which you can specify whether the block parameters will be stored in a separate data block (single instance) or as a local tag (multiple instance) in the block interface. If you create a separate data block, you will find it in the project tree in the "Program resources" folder under "Program blocks &gt; System blocks". For additional information on this topic, refer to "See also".

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Compare input bits with the bits of a mask" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| IN_BIT0 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 0 is compared with bit 0 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT1 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 1 is compared with bit 1 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT2 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 2 is compared with bit 2 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT3 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 3 is compared with bit 3 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT4 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 4 is compared with bit 4 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT5 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 5 is compared with bit 5 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT6 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 6 is compared with bit 6 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT7 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 7 is compared with bit 7 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT8 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 8 is compared with bit 8 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT9 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 9 is compared with bit 9 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT10 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 10 is compared with bit 10 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT11 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 11 is compared with bit 11 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT12 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 12 is compared with bit 12 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT13 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 13 is compared with bit 13 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT14 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 14 is compared with bit 14 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT15 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 15 is compared with bit 15 of the mask. |
| CMP_STEP | Input | BYTE | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | The step number of the mask used for the comparison. |
| OUT | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | The signal state "1" indicates that a match was found.  A signal state of "0" indicates that no match was found. |
| ERR_CODE | Output | WORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Error information |
| CMP_VAL | Static | ARRAY of BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Comparison masks [0 to 15, 0 to 15]: The first number of the index is the step number and the second number is the bit number of the mask. |

For additional information on valid data types, refer to "See also".

#### ERR_CODE parameter

The following table shows the meaning of the values of the ERR_CODE parameter:

| Error code* (W#16#...) | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| 0000 | No error |
| 000A | The value at the CMP_STEP parameter is greater than 15. |
| *The error codes can be displayed as integer or hexadecimal value in the program editor. You can find information on switching the display formats here: [Switching display formats in the program status](Testing%20the%20user%20program.md#switching-display-formats-in-the-program-status) |  |

#### Example

In the following example all 16 input bits are compared with the mask for step 2. The signal state of the OUT parameter is set to TRUE, since the input bits match the mask for step 2.

> **Note**
>
> You can initialize static parameters in the data block.

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| CALL IMC, "IMC_DB" | // The instruction is called and the instance data block "IMC_DB" is created. |
| IN_BIT0 := "Tag_Input_BIT0" | // Input bit 0 |
| IN_BIT1 := "Tag_Input_BIT1" | // Input bit 1 |
| IN_BIT2 := "Tag_Input_BIT2" | // Input bit 2 |
| IN_BIT3 := "Tag_Input_BIT3" | // Input bit 3 |
| IN_BIT4 := "Tag_Input_BIT4" | // Input bit 4 |
| IN_BIT5 := "Tag_Input_BIT5" | // Input bit 5 |
| IN_BIT6 := "Tag_Input_BIT6" | // Input bit 6 |
| IN_BIT7 := "Tag_Input_BIT7" | // Input bit 7 |
| IN_BIT8 := "Tag_Input_BIT8" | // Input bit 8 |
| IN_BIT9 := "Tag_Input_BIT9" | // Input bit 9 |
| IN_BIT10 := "Tag_Input_BIT10" | // Input bit 10 |
| IN_BIT11 := "Tag_Input_BIT11" | // Input bit 11 |
| IN_BIT12 := "Tag_Input_BIT12" | // Input bit 12 |
| IN_BIT13 := "Tag_Input_BIT13" | // Input bit 13 |
| IN_BIT14 := "Tag_Input_BIT14" | // Input bit 14 |
| IN_BIT15 := "Tag_Input_BIT15" | // Input bit 15 |
| CMP_STEP := "Tag_CMP_STEP" | // Step number of the mask |
| OUT := "Tag_Output" | // Indicates whether or not a match was found |
| ERR_CODE := "Tag_ErrorCode" | // Error information |

The following tables show how the instruction works using specific values.

#### Before processing

In this example, the following values are used for the input and output parameters:

| Parameters | Operand | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| IN_BIT0 | Tag_Input_BIT0 | TRUE |
| IN_BIT1 | Tag_Input_BIT1 | TRUE |
| IN_BIT2 | Tag_Input_BIT2 | FALSE |
| IN_BIT3 | Tag_Input_BIT3 | TRUE |
| IN_BIT4 | Tag_Input_BIT4 | TRUE |
| IN_BIT5 | Tag_Input_BIT5 | FALSE |
| IN_BIT6 | Tag_Input_BIT6 | TRUE |
| IN_BIT7 | Tag_Input_BIT7 | TRUE |
| IN_BIT8 | Tag_Input_BIT8 | FALSE |
| IN_BIT9 | Tag_Input_BIT9 | TRUE |
| IN_BIT10 | Tag_Input_BIT10 | TRUE |

| IN_BIT12 | Tag_Input_BIT12 | TRUE |
| IN_BIT13 | Tag_Input_BIT13 | TRUE |

| IN_BIT15 | Tag_Input_BIT15 | TRUE |
| CMP_STEP | Tag_CMP_STEP | B#16#02 |
| OUT | Tag_Output | FALSE |
| ERR_CODE | Tag_ErrorCode | W#16#0000 |

| --- | --- | --- |

### SMC: Compare scan matrix (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

You can use the "Compare scan matrix" instruction to compare the signal state of up to 16 programmed input bits (IN_BIT0 to IN_BIT15) with the corresponding bit of the comparison masks for each step. Processing starts at step 1 and is continued until the last programmed step (LAST) or until a match is found. The input bit of the IN_BIT0 parameter is compared with the value of the mask CMP_VAL[x,0], with "x" indicating the step number. All programmed values are compared in the same manner. If a match is found the signal state of the OUT parameter is set to "1" and the step number with the matching mask is written in the OUT_STEP parameter. Unprogrammed input bits or unprogrammed bits of the mask have a default signal state FALSE. If more than one step has a matching mask, only the first one found is indicated in the OUT_STEP parameter. If no match is found, the signal state of the OUT parameter is set to "0". In this case the value at the OUT_STEP parameter is greater by "1" than the value at the LAST parameter.

When you insert the instruction in the program, the "Call options" dialog opens in which you can specify whether the block parameters will be stored in a separate data block (single instance) or as a local tag (multiple instance) in the block interface. If you create a separate data block, you will find it in the project tree in the "Program resources" folder under "Program blocks &gt; System blocks". For additional information on this topic, refer to "See also".

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Compare scan matrix" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| IN_BIT0 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 0 is compared with bit 0 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT1 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 1 is compared with bit 1 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT2 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 2 is compared with bit 2 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT3 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 3 is compared with bit 3 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT4 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 4 is compared with bit 4 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT5 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 5 is compared with bit 5 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT6 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 6 is compared with bit 6 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT7 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 7 is compared with bit 7 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT8 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 8 is compared with bit 8 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT9 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 9 is compared with bit 9 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT10 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 10 is compared with bit 10 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT11 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 11 is compared with bit 11 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT12 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 12 is compared with bit 12 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT13 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 13 is compared with bit 13 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT14 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 14 is compared with bit 14 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT15 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 15 is compared with bit 15 of the mask. |
| OUT | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | The signal state "1" indicates that a match was found.  A signal state of "0" indicates that no match was found. |
| ERR_CODE | Output | WORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Error information |
| OUT_STEP | Output | BYTE | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Contains the step number with the matching mask or the step number which is greater by "1" than the value of the LAST parameter, provided no match is found. |
| LAST | Static | BYTE | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Specifies the step number of the last step to be scanned for a matching mask. |
| CMP_VAL | Static | ARRAY of WORD | I, Q, M, D, L | Comparison masks [0 to 15, 0 to 15]: The first number of the index is the step number and the second number is the bit number of the mask. |

For additional information on valid data types, refer to "See also".

#### ERR_CODE parameter

The following table shows the meaning of the values of the ERR_CODE parameter:

| Error code* (W#16#...) | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| 0000 | No error |
| 000E | The value at the LAST parameter is greater than 15. |
| *The error codes can be displayed as integer or hexadecimal value in the program editor. You can find information on switching the display formats here: [Switching display formats in the program status](Testing%20the%20user%20program.md#switching-display-formats-in-the-program-status) |  |

#### Example

In this example, all 16 input bits are compared with the mask for steps 0 through 5 until a match is found. Only the masks for steps 0 through 2 are scanned, since the mask for step 2 matches the input bit.

> **Note**
>
> You can initialize static parameters in the data block.

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| CALL SMC, "SMC_DB" | // The instruction is called and the instance data block "SMC_DB" is created. |
| IN_BIT0 := "Tag_Input_BIT0" | // Input bit 0 |
| IN_BIT1 := "Tag_Input_BIT1" | // Input bit 1 |
| IN_BIT2 := "Tag_Input_BIT2" | // Input bit 2 |
| IN_BIT3 := "Tag_Input_BIT3" | // Input bit 3 |
| IN_BIT4 := "Tag_Input_BIT4" | // Input bit 4 |
| IN_BIT5 := "Tag_Input_BIT5" | // Input bit 5 |
| IN_BIT6 := "Tag_Input_BIT6" | // Input bit 6 |
| IN_BIT7 := "Tag_Input_BIT7" | // Input bit 7 |
| IN_BIT8 := "Tag_Input_BIT8" | // Input bit 8 |
| IN_BIT9 := "Tag_Input_BIT9" | // Input bit 9 |
| IN_BIT10 := "Tag_Input_BIT10" | // Input bit 10 |

| IN_BIT14 := "Tag_Input_BIT14" | // Input bit 14 |
| IN_BIT15 := "Tag_Input_BIT15" | // Input bit 15 |
| OUT := "Tag_Output" | // Indicates whether or not a match was found. |
| OUT_STEP := "Tag_Output_STEP" | // Contains the step number with the relevant mask. |
| ERR_CODE := "Tag_ErrorCode" | // Error information |

The following tables show how the instruction works using specific values.

### LEAD_LAG: Lead and lag algorithm  (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

You can use the "Lead and lag algorithm" instruction to process signals with an analog tag. The gain value at the GAIN parameter must be greater than zero. The result of the "Lead and lag algorithm" instruction is calculated using the following equation:

![Description](images/49016018315_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

The "Lead and lag algorithm" instruction supplies plausible results only when processing is in fixed program cycles. The same units must be specified at the parameters LD_TIME, LG_TIME and SAMPLE_T. At LG_TIME &gt; 4 + SAMPLE_T, the instruction approaches the following function:

OUT = GAIN * ((1 + LD_TIME * s) / (1 + LG_TIME * s)) * IN

When the value of the GAIN parameter is less than or equal to zero, the calculation is not performed and an error information is output on the ERR_CODE parameter.

You can use the instruction "Lead and lag algorithm" in conjunction with loops as a compensator in dynamic feed-forward control. The instruction consists of two operations. The "Lead" operation shifts the phase of the OUT output so that the output leads the input. The "Lag" operation, on the other hand, shifts the output so that the output lags behind the input. Because the "Lag" operation is equivalent to an integration, it can be used as a noise suppressor or as a low-pass filter. The "Lead" operation is equivalent to a differentiation and can therefore be used as a high-pass filter. The two instructions together (Lead and Lag) result in the output phase lagging behind the input at lower frequencies and leading it at higher frequencies. This means that the "Lead and lag algorithm" instruction can be used as a band pass filter.

When you insert the instruction in the program, the "Call options" dialog opens in which you can specify whether the block parameters will be stored in a separate data block (single instance) or as a local tag (multiple instance) in the block interface. If you create a separate data block, you will find it in the project tree in the "Program resources" folder under "Program blocks &gt; System blocks". For additional information on this topic, refer to "See also".

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Lead and lag algorithm" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| IN | Input | REAL | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | The input value of the current sample time (cycle time) to be processed. |
| SAMPLE_T | Input | INT | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | Sample time |
| OUT | Output | REAL | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Result of the instruction |
| ERR_CODE | Output | WORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Error information |
| LD_TIME | Static | REAL | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | Lead time in the same unit as sample time. |
| LG_TIME | Static | REAL | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | Lag time in the same unit as sample time |
| GAIN | Static | REAL | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | Gain as % / % (the ratio of the change in output to a change in input as a steady state). |
| PREV_IN | Static | REAL | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | Previous input |
| PREV_OUT | Static | REAL | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | Previous output |

For additional information on valid data types, refer to "See also".

#### ERR_CODE parameter

The following table shows the meaning of the values of the ERR_CODE parameter:

| Error code* (W#16#...) | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| 0000 | No error |
| 0009 | The value at the GAIN parameter is less than or equal to zero. |
| *The error codes can be displayed as integer or hexadecimal value in the program editor. You can find information on switching the display formats here: [Switching display formats in the program status](Testing%20the%20user%20program.md#switching-display-formats-in-the-program-status) |  |

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

> **Note**
>
> You can initialize static parameters in the data block.

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| CALL LEAD_LAG, "LEAD_LAG_DB" | // The instruction is called and the instance data block "LEAD_LAG_DB" is created. |
| IN := "Tag_Input" | // The input value of the current sample time (cycle time) to be processed. |
| SAMPLE_T := "Tag_Input_SAMPE_T" | // Sample time |
| OUT := "Tag_Output_Result" | // Result of the instruction |
| ERR_CODE := "Tag_ErrorCode" | // Error information |

The following tables show how the instruction works using specific values.

#### Before processing

In this example the following values are used for the input parameters:

| Parameters | Operand | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| IN | Tag_Input | 2.0 |
| SAMPLE_T | Tag_InputSampleTime | 10 |

The following values are saved in the "LEAD_LAG_DB" instance data block of the instruction:

| Parameters | Address | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| LD_TIME | DBD12 | 2.0 |
| LG_TIME | DBD16 | 2.0 |
| GAIN | DBD20 | 1.0 |
| PREV_IN | DBD24 | 6.0 |
| PREV_OUT | DBD28 | 6.0 |

#### After processing

The following values are written to the output parameters after the instruction has been executed:

| Parameters | Operand | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| OUT | Tag_Output_Result | 2.0 |

The following values are saved in the instance data block "LEAD_LAD_DB" of the instruction:

| Parameters | Operand | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| PREV_IN | DBD24 | 2.0 |
| PREV_OUT | DBD28 | 2.0 |

### TONR_X: Time accumulator (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

You use the "Time accumulator" instruction to accumulate time values within a period which you set using the PV input. The instruction is executed when the signal state on the TMR_EN start input changes from "0" to "1". Simultaneously, the timer runs for the duration set at the PV input. While the instruction is being executed, it adds the time value of the DELTA_T input to the time value of the InOut ET.

The following conditions must be met:

- The TMR_EN start input has the signal state "1".
- The time value at InOut ET is less than the time value at the PV parameter.
- The RESET input has the signal state "0".

The instruction is interrupted when the signal state on the TMR_EN start input changes from "1" to "0". As soon as the signal state changes back to "1", the instruction resumes execution.

The instruction is ended when the time value at InOut ET has reached the time value at the PV input. The Q output then has the signal state "1".

As long as the Q output has the signal state "1", the time value at InOut ET remains unchanged. The time value and the Q output are not reset to "0" until the RESET input is set to signal state "1".

Since the "Time accumulator" instruction uses the cycle time (DELTA_T) of the last cycle of the organization block (OB), the instruction may only be called in cyclic organization blocks.

> **Note**
>
> You have to move the cycle time of the organization block from the startup information to the global tag of the DELTA_T parameter.

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Time accumulator" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| TMR_EN (Timer Enable) | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Start input  Starts the instruction and the expiration of the preset time duration at the PV input |
| RESET | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Reset input |
| PV (Preset Value) | Input | DINT | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | Maximum duration of time recording |
| DELTA_T | Input | INT | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | Cycle time of organization block of the previous cycle |
| Q | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Output which is set when the preset time value is reached |
| ET (Elapsed Time) | InOut | DINT | I, Q, M, D, L | Accumulated time value  (Currently elapsed time value + time value of the DELTA_T input) |

For additional information on valid data types, refer to "See also".

#### Pulse timing diagram

The following figure shows the pulse timing diagram of the "Time accumulator" instruction:

![Pulse timing diagram](images/65905837067_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| CALL TONR_X | // The instruction is called. |
| TMR_EN := "Tag_Start" | // Start input |
| RESET := "Tag_Reset" | // Reset input |
| PV := 10 | // Maximum duration of time recording |
| DELTA_T := 2 | // Cycle time of organization block of the previous cycle |
| ET := "Tag_Elapsed_Time" | // Accumulated time |
| Q := "Tag_Output" | // Indicates whether the time set for the PV parameter has been reached. |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)
