[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[STL programming examples (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#stl-programming-examples-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

### Comparator operations (S7-300, S7-400)

This section contains information on the following topics:

- [? I: Compare 16-bit integers (S7-300, S7-400)](#i-compare-16-bit-integers-s7-300-s7-400)
- [? D: Compare 32-bit integers (S7-300, S7-400)](#d-compare-32-bit-integers-s7-300-s7-400)
- [? R: Compare floating-point numbers (S7-300, S7-400)](#r-compare-floating-point-numbers-s7-300-s7-400)

#### ? I: Compare 16-bit integers (S7-300, S7-400)

##### Description

With the "Compare 16-bit integers" instruction you compare the content of the right word in accumulator 2 with the content of the right word in accumulator 1. The contents of accumulators 1 and 2 are interpreted as 16-bit integers. The instruction performs the comparison depending on the specified comparison function.

The following table shows the available comparison functions and their meaning:

| Comparison function | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| ==I | Compare 16-bit integers for "equivalence" |
| &lt;&gt;I | Compare 16-bit integers for "non-equivalence" |
| &gt;I | Compare 16-bit integers for "greater than" |
| &lt;I | Compare 16-bit integers for "less than" |
| &gt;=I | Compare 16-bit integers for "greater than or equal to" |
| &lt;=I | Compare 16-bit integers for "less than or equal to" |

The result of the comparison influences the result of logic operation (RLO) and the status bits CC 1 and CC 0. If the condition of the comparison is satisfied, the RLO is set to signal state "1". When the condition of the comparison is not met, the RLO is set to signal state "0".

The following table shows how the various comparison functions affect the RLO:

| Comparison function | RLO if  ACCU 2 &gt; ACCU 1 | RLO if  ACCU 2 = ACCU 1 | RLO if  ACCU 2 &lt; ACCU 1 |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| ==I | 0 | 1 | 0 |
| &lt;&gt;I | 1 | 0 | 1 |
| &gt;I | 1 | 0 | 0 |
| &lt;I | 0 | 0 | 1 |
| &gt;=I | 1 | 1 | 0 |
| &lt;=I | 0 | 1 | 1 |

The setting of status bits CC 1 and CC 0 depends on the relationship between the two values involved in the comparison.

The contents of accumulators 1 and 2 are not changed by execution of the comparison functions. After the processing of a comparison function you can evaluate the result of the logic operation with assignment and jump functions.

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Input_1" | // Load value of the operand "Tag_Input_1" in accumulator 1 |
| L "Tag_Input_2" | // Shift the contents of accumulator 1 (Tag_Input_1) to accumulator 2.  // Load value of the operand "Tag_Input_2" in accumulator 1 |
| &gt;I | // Compare whether the value of the operand "Tag_Input_1" is greater than the value of the operand "Tag_Input_2". |
| = "Tag_Output" | // Assign result of the comparison to the operand "Tag_Output". |

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Operand | Values |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Tag_Input_1 | 10 | 10 | 5 |
| Tag_Input_2 | 5 | 10 | 10 |
| Tag_Output | 1 | 0 | 0 |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)

[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[STL programming examples (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#stl-programming-examples-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

#### ? D: Compare 32-bit integers (S7-300, S7-400)

##### Description

Use the instruction "Compare 32-bit integers" to compare the contents of accumulator 2 (ACCU 2) with the contents of accumulator 1 (ACCU 1). The contents of accumulators 1 and 2 are interpreted as 32-bit integers. The instruction performs the comparison depending on the specified comparison function.

The following table shows the available comparison functions and their meaning:

| Comparison function | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| ==D | Compare 32-bit integers for "equivalence" |
| &lt;&gt;D | Compare 32-bit integers for "non-equivalence" |
| &gt;D | Compare 32-bit integers for "greater than" |
| &lt;D | Compare 32-bit integers for "less than" |
| &gt;=D | Compare 32-bit integers for "greater than or equal to" |
| &lt;=D | Compare 32-bit integers for "less than or equal to" |

The result of the comparison influences the result of logic operation (RLO) and the status bits CC 1 and CC 0. If the condition of the comparison is satisfied, the RLO is set to signal state "1". If the condition of the comparison is not met, the RLO is reset to signal state "0".

The following table shows how the various comparison functions affect the RLO:

| Comparison function | RLO if  ACCU 2 &gt; ACCU 1 | RLO if  ACCU 2 = ACCU 1 | RLO if  ACCU 2 &lt; ACCU 1 |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| ==D | 0 | 1 | 0 |
| &lt;&gt;D | 1 | 0 | 1 |
| &gt;D | 1 | 0 | 0 |
| &lt;D | 0 | 0 | 1 |
| &gt;=D | 1 | 1 | 0 |
| &lt;=D | 0 | 1 | 1 |

The setting of status bits CC 1 and CC 0 depends on the relationship between the two values involved in the comparison.

The contents of accumulators 1 and 2 are not changed by execution of the comparison functions. After the processing of a comparison function, you can evaluate the result of the logic operation with assignment and jump functions.

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Input_1" | // Load value of the operand "Tag_Input_1" in accumulator 1 |
| L "Tag_Input_2" | // Contents of accumulator 1 (Tag_Input_1) shifted to accumulator 2.  // Load value of the operand "Tag_Input_2" in accumulator 1 |
| &gt;D | // Compare whether the value of the operand "Tag_Input_1" is greater than the value of the operand "Tag_Input_2". |
| = "Tag_Output" | // Assign result of the comparison to the operand "Tag_Output". |

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Operand | Values |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Tag_Input_1 | 150 000 | 150 000 | 100 000 |
| Tag_Input_2 | 100 000 | 150 000 | 150 000 |
| Tag_Output | 1 | 0 | 0 |

---

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)

#### ? R: Compare floating-point numbers (S7-300, S7-400)

##### Description

Use the instruction "Compare floating-point numbers" to compare the contents of accumulator 2 (ACCU 2) with the contents of accumulator 1 (ACCU 1). The contents of accumulators 1 and 2 are interpreted as floating-point numbers. For the comparison, accumulators 1 and 2 must contain valid floating-point numbers. The instruction performs the comparison depending on the specified comparison function.

The following table shows the available comparison functions and their meaning:

| Comparison function | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| ==R | Compare floating-point numbers for "equivalence" |
| &lt;&gt;R | Compare floating-point numbers for "non-equivalence" |
| &gt;R | Compare floating-point numbers for "greater than" |
| &lt;R | Compare floating-point numbers for "less than" |
| &gt;=R | Compare floating-point numbers for "greater than or equal to" |
| &lt;=R | Compare floating-point numbers for "less than or equal to" |

The result of the comparison influences the result of logic operation (RLO) and the status bits CC 1 and CC 0. If the condition of the comparison is satisfied, the RLO is set to signal state "1". If the condition of the comparison is not met, the RLO is reset to signal state "0".

The following table shows how the various comparison functions affect the RLO:

| Comparison function | RLO if  ACCU 2 &gt; ACCU 1 | RLO if  ACCU 2 = ACCU 1 | RLO if  ACCU 2 &lt; ACCU 1 |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| ==R | 0 | 1 | 0 |
| &lt;&gt;R | 1 | 0 | 1 |
| &gt;R | 1 | 0 | 0 |
| &lt;R | 0 | 0 | 1 |
| &gt;=R | 1 | 1 | 0 |
| &lt;=R | 0 | 1 | 1 |

The setting of status bits CC 1 and CC 0 depends on the relationship between the two values involved in the comparison.

> **Note**
>
> During a comparison of invalid floating-point numbers, the CPU sets the result of logic operation to "0" and the status bits CC 0, CC 1, OVand OS to "1".

The contents of accumulators 1 and 2 are not changed by execution of the comparison functions. After the processing of a comparison function you can evaluate the result of the logic operation with assignment and jump functions.

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Input_1" | // Load value of the operand "Tag_Input_1" in accumulator 1 |
| L "Tag_Input_2" | // Shift the contents of accumulator 1 (Tag_Input_1) to accumulator 2.  // Load value of the operand "Tag_Input_2" in accumulator 1 |
| &gt;R | // Compare whether the value of the operand "Tag_Input_1" is greater than the value of the operand "Tag_Input_2". |
| = "Tag_Output" | // Assign result of the comparison to the operand "Tag_Output". |

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Operand | Values |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Tag_Input_1 | 10 515 | 10 515 | 5 232 |
| Tag_Input_2 | 5 232 | 10 515 | 10 515 |
| Tag_Output | 1 | 0 | 0 |

---

#### Integers (S7-300, S7-400)

This section contains information on the following topics:

- [+I: Add integers (16 bit) (S7-300, S7-400)](#i-add-integers-16-bit-s7-300-s7-400)
- [-I: Subtract integers (16 bit) (S7-300, S7-400)](#i-subtract-integers-16-bit-s7-300-s7-400)

- [/I: Divide integers (16 bit) (S7-300, S7-400)](#i-divide-integers-16-bit-s7-300-s7-400)
- [+D: Add double integers (32 bit) (S7-300, S7-400)](#d-add-double-integers-32-bit-s7-300-s7-400)
- [-D: Subtract double integers (32 bit) (S7-300, S7-400)](#d-subtract-double-integers-32-bit-s7-300-s7-400)
- [*D: Multiply double integers (32 bit) (S7-300, S7-400)](#d-multiply-double-integers-32-bit-s7-300-s7-400)
- [/D: Divide double integers (32 bit) (S7-300, S7-400)](#d-divide-double-integers-32-bit-s7-300-s7-400)

- [DEC: Decrement (S7-300, S7-400)](#dec-decrement-s7-300-s7-400)

##### +I: Add integers (16 bit) (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the instruction "Add integers (16 bit)" to add the values in the right words of accumulators 1 and 2. The instruction interprets these values as 16-bit integers.

The instruction saves the sum in the right word of accumulator 1. The left word of accumulator 1 remains unchanged.

After the instruction has executed, the status bits CC 0 and CC 1 indicate whether the sum is negative, zero or positive. If the number is outside the permitted number range, the status bits OV and OS are set to "1".

In case of controllers with two accumulators the content of accumulator 2 remains unchanged after processing of the instruction.

In case of controllers with four accumulators the contents of accumulator 3 are copied to accumulator 2 and the contents of accumulator 4 are copied to accumulator 3. The contents of accumulator 4 remain unchanged after the instruction has executed.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load first value for addition. |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Load second value for addition. |
| +I | // Add values |
| T "Tag_Result" | // Transfer sum to the operand "Tag_Result". |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)

##### -I: Subtract integers (16 bit) (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

With the "Subtract integers (16 bit)" instruction you subtract the value of the right word of accumulator 1 from the value of the right word of accumulator 2. The instruction interprets the values of accumulators 1 and 2 as 16-bit integers.

The instruction saves the difference in the right word of accumulator 1. The left word of accumulator 1 remains unchanged.

After the instruction has executed, the status bits CC 0 and CC 1 indicate whether the difference is negative, zero or positive. If the number is outside the permitted number range, the status bits OV and OS are set to "1".

In case of controllers with two accumulators the content of accumulator 2 remains unchanged after processing of the instruction.

In case of controllers with four accumulators the contents of accumulator 3 are copied to accumulator 2 and the contents of accumulator 4 are copied to accumulator 3. The contents of accumulator 4 remain unchanged after the instruction has executed.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load first value of subtraction into accumulator 1. |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Shift the contents of accumulator 1 to accumulator 2.  // Load second value for addition in accumulator 1. |
| -I | // Subtract value of accumulator 1 from value of accumulator 2. |
| T "Tag_Result" | // Transfer difference to the operand "Tag_Result". |

---

[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[STL programming examples (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#stl-programming-examples-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

##### *I: Multiply integers (16 bit) (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the instruction "Multiply integers (16 bit)" to multiply the values in the right words of accumulators 1 and 2. The instruction interprets these values as 16-bit integers.

The instruction saves the product in accumulator 1 as 32-bit integer (DINT).

After the instruction has executed, the status bits CC 0 and CC 1 indicate whether the product is negative, zero or positive. If the number is outside the permitted number range, the status bits OV and OS are set to "1".

In case of controllers with two accumulators the content of accumulator 2 remains unchanged after processing of the instruction.

In case of controllers with four accumulators the contents of accumulator 3 are copied to accumulator 2 and the contents of accumulator 4 are copied to accumulator 3. The contents of accumulator 4 remain unchanged after the instruction has executed.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load first value for multiplication. |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Load second value for multiplication. |
| *I | // Multiply values |
| T "Tag_Result" | // Transfer product to the operand "Tag_Result". |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)

[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[STL programming examples (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#stl-programming-examples-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

##### /I: Divide integers (16 bit) (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

With the "Divide integers (16 bit)" instruction you divide the contents of the right word in accumulator 2 by the contents of the right word in accumulator 1. The instruction interprets the values of the accumulators as 16-bit integers.

The instruction provides two results: the quotients and the remainder of the division. The quotient is the whole number result of the division. The instruction saves this in the right word of accumulator 1. The instruction saves the remainder of the division in the left word of accumulator 1. If the dividend is negative, the remainder of the division is also negative.

After the instruction has executed, the status bits CC 0 and CC 1 indicate whether the quotient is negative, zero or positive. If the number is outside the permitted number range, the status bits OV and OS are set to "1".

In the case of a division by zero, the instruction reports the value as quotient and in each case the value zero as remainder. In this case, status bits CC 0, CC 1, OV and OS are set to signal state "1".

In case of controllers with two accumulators the content of accumulator 2 remains unchanged after processing of the instruction.

In case of controllers with four accumulators the contents of accumulator 3 are copied to accumulator 2 and the contents of accumulator 4 are copied to accumulator 3. The contents of accumulator 4 remain unchanged after the instruction has executed.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load dividend in accumulator 1. |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Move dividend to accumulator 2.  // Load divisor in accumulator 1. |
| /I | // Divide the value of accumulator 2 by the value of accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Result" | // Transfer the result to operand "Tag_Result". |

###### Before processing

The following table shows the contents of the right words in accumulators 1 and 2 before executing the "Divide integers (16 bit)" instruction:

| Accumulator | Value |
| --- | --- |
| Accumulator 2 | 13 |
| Accumulator 1 | 4 |

###### After processing

The following table shows the contents of accumulator 1 after executing the "Divide integers (16 bit)" instruction:

| Accumulator 1 | Value |
| --- | --- |
| Bit 0 to 15 (right word) | 3 |
| Bit 16 to 31 (left word) | 1 |

---

##### +D: Add double integers (32 bit) (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Add double integers (32 bit)" instruction to add the values in accumulators 1 and 2. The instruction interprets these values as 32-bit integers. The instruction saves the sum in accumulator 1.

After the instruction has executed, the status bits CC 0 and CC 1 indicate whether the sum is negative, zero or positive. If the number is outside the permitted number range, the status bits OV and OS are set to "1".

In case of controllers with two accumulators the content of accumulator 2 remains unchanged after processing of the instruction.

In case of controllers with four accumulators the contents of accumulator 3 are copied to accumulator 2 and the contents of accumulator 4 are copied to accumulator 3. The contents of accumulator 4 remain unchanged after the instruction has executed.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load first value for addition. |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Load second value for addition. |
| +D | // Add values |
| T "Tag_Result" | // Transfer sum to the operand "Tag_Result". |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)

[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

##### -D: Subtract double integers (32 bit) (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

With the "Subtract double integers (32 bit)" instruction you subtract the value of accumulator 1 from the value of accumulator 2. The instruction interprets the values of accumulators 1 and 2 as 32-bit double integers. The instruction saves the result of the subtraction in accumulator 1.

After the instruction has executed, the status bits CC 0 and CC 1 indicate whether the difference is negative, zero or positive. If the number is outside the permitted number range, the status bits OV and OS are set to "1".

In case of controllers with two accumulators the content of accumulator 2 remains unchanged after processing of the instruction.

In case of controllers with four accumulators the contents of accumulator 3 are copied to accumulator 2 and the contents of accumulator 4 are copied to accumulator 3. The contents of accumulator 4 remain unchanged after the instruction has executed.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load first value of subtraction into accumulator 1. |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Shift the contents of accumulator 1 to accumulator 2.  // Load the second value of subtraction into accumulator 1. |
| -D | // Subtract value of accumulator 1 from value of accumulator 2. |
| T "Tag_Result" | // Transfer difference to the operand "Tag_Result". |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)

##### *D: Multiply double integers (32 bit) (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Multiply double integers (32 bit)" instruction to multiply the values in accumulators 1 and 2. The instruction interprets these values as 32-bit integers. The instruction saves the product in accumulator 1.

After the instruction has executed, the status bits CC 0 and CC 1 indicate whether the product is negative, zero or positive. If the number is outside the permitted number range, the status bits OV and OS are set to "1".

In case of controllers with two accumulators the content of accumulator 2 remains unchanged after processing of the instruction.

In case of controllers with four accumulators the contents of accumulator 3 are copied to accumulator 2 and the contents of accumulator 4 are copied to accumulator 3. The contents of accumulator 4 remain unchanged after the instruction has executed.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load first value for multiplication. |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Load second value for multiplication. |
| *D | // Multiply values |
| T "Tag_Result" | // Transfer product to the operand "Tag_Result". |

##### /D: Divide double integers (32 bit) (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

With the "Divide double integers (32 bit)" instruction you divide the value of accumulator 2 by the value of accumulator 1. The instruction interprets the values of accumulators 1 and 2 as 32-bit double integers. The instruction saves the result of the division (quotient) in accumulator 1.

After the instruction has executed, the status bits CC 0 and CC 1 indicate whether the quotient is negative, zero or positive. If the number is outside the permitted number range, the status bits OV and OS are set to "1".

In the case of a division by zero, the instruction reports the value zero as quotient. In this case, status bits CC 0, CC 1, OV and OS are set to signal state "1".

In case of controllers with two accumulators the content of accumulator 2 remains unchanged after processing of the instruction.

In case of controllers with four accumulators the contents of accumulator 3 are copied to accumulator 2 and the contents of accumulator 4 are copied to accumulator 3. The contents of accumulator 4 remain unchanged after the instruction has executed.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load dividend in accumulator 1. |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Move dividend to accumulator 2.  // Load divisor in accumulator 1. |
| /D | // Divide the value of accumulator 2 by the value of accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Result" | // Transfer quotients to the operand "Tag_Result". |

###### Before processing

The following table shows the contents of accumulators 1 and 2 before executing the "Divide double integers (32 bit)" instruction:

| Accumulator | Value |
| --- | --- |
| Accumulator 2 | 13 |
| Accumulator 1 | 4 |

###### After processing

The following table shows the contents of accumulator 1 after executing the "Divide double integers (32 bit)" instruction:

| Accumulator | Value |
| --- | --- |
| Accumulator 1 | 3 |

[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

##### +: Add constants (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

With the "Add constants" instruction, you add the value of a specified constant to the contents of accumulator 1. You can specify the constant value as 16-bit integer or 32-bit double integer. The instruction stores the result in accumulator 1. When adding 16-bit integers, the instruction only influences the right word of accumulator 1.

To execute the addition of a 16-bit integer as DINT math function, enter "L#" before the constant. The "Add constants" instruction permits the use of negative numbers.

The instruction does not affect any status bits.

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Add constants" instruction:

| Parameters | Data type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;constant&gt; | INT, DINT | Constants to be added |

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_1". |
| + 25 | // Increment the value of accumulator 1 by 25. |
| T "Tag_Result_1" | // Transfer contents of accumulator 1 to the operand "Tag_Result_1". |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_2" in accumulator 1 |
| L "Tag_Value_3" | // Shift the contents of accumulator 1 to accumulator 2.  // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_3" in accumulator 1 |
| + -100 | // Decrement the value of accumulator 1 by 100. |
| &lt;I | // Check whether the value of accumulator 2 is less than the value of accumulator 1 |
| JC NEXT | // If the result of the query is "1", jump to jump label NEXT .  // If the result of the query is "0", execute the next instruction. |
| T "Tag_Result_2" | Transfer contents of accumulator 1 to the operand "Tag_Result_2". |
| L "Tag_Value_4" | // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_4". |
| + L#20 | // Increment content of accumulator 1 by 20.  // The addition is done as a DINT calculation |
| T "Tag_Result_3" | // Transfer contents of accumulator 1 to the operand "Tag_Result_3". |
| NEXT: L "Tag_Value_5" | // Jump label "NEXT"  // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_5". |
| +D | // Add values of accumulators 1 and 2. |
| T "Tag_Result_4" | // Transfer sum to the operand "Tag_Result_4". |

---

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)

[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

##### INC: Increment (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Increment" instruction to increment the value in accumulator 1 by the value specified as parameter of the instruction. The specified value can be in a value range from 0 to 255. The value is incremented only in the right byte of accumulator 1. There is no transfer to the byte located on the left.

The CPU executes the instruction regardless of the result of logic operation and the status bit. The instruction does not affect either the result of logic operation or the status bit.

The contents of accumulator 2, 3 and 4 remain unchanged.

If the parameter value is outside the permitted range of value, the result will be corrupted without generating an error message.

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Increment" instruction:

| Parameters | Format | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;constant&gt; | 8-bit integer | Value by which the value is incremented. |

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value" | // Load value of the operand in accumulator 1. |
| INC 5 | // Increment value of accumulator 1 by 5. |
| T "Tag_Result" | // Transfer contents of accumulator 1 to the operand. |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)
  
[Address areas of the CPUs (S7-300, S7-400)](Functional%20description%20of%20S7-300-400%20CPUs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%29.md#address-areas-of-the-cpus-s7-300-s7-400)

[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

##### DEC: Decrement (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Decrement" instruction to decrement the value in accumulator 1 by the value specified as parameter of the instruction. The specified value can be in a value range from 0 to 255. The value is decremented only in the right byte of accumulator 1. There is no transfer to the byte located on the left.

The CPU executes the instruction regardless of the result of logic operation and the status bit. The instruction does not affect either the result of logic operation or the status bit.

The contents of accumulator 2, 3 and 4 remain unchanged.

If the parameter value is outside the permitted range of value, the result will be corrupted without generating an error message.

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Decrement" instruction:

| Parameters | Format | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;constant&gt; | 8-bit integer | Value by which the value is decremented. |

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value" | // Load value of the operand in accumulator 1. |
| DEC 5 | // Decrement the value of accumulator 1 by 5. |
| T "Tag_Result" | // Transfer contents of accumulator 1 to the operand. |

---

[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

##### MOD: Return remainder of division (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Return remainder of division" instruction to divide the value of accumulator 2 by the value of accumulator 1 and save the remainder of the division.

The instruction interprets the values of accumulators 1 and 2 as 32-bit integers. The instruction stores the remainder of the division in accumulator 1.

After the instruction has executed, the status bits CC 0 and CC 1 indicate whether the remainder of division is negative, zero or positive. If the number is outside the permitted number range, the status bits OV and OS are set to "1".

In the case of a division by zero, the instruction returns the value zero as result. In this case, status bits CC 0, CC 1, OV and OS are set to signal state "1".

In case of controllers with two accumulators the content of accumulator 2 remains unchanged after processing of the instruction.

In case of controllers with four accumulators the contents of accumulator 3 are copied to accumulator 2 and the contents of accumulator 4 are copied to accumulator 3. The contents of accumulator 4 remain unchanged after the instruction has executed.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load dividend in accumulator 1. |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Move dividend to accumulator 2.  // Load divisor in accumulator 1. |
| MOD | // Divide the value of accumulator 2 by the value of accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Result" | // Transfer remainder of division to the operand "Tag_Result". |

###### Before processing

The following table shows the contents of accumulators 1 and 2 before executing the instruction "Return remainder of division":

| Accumulator | Value |
| --- | --- |
| Accumulator 2 | 13 |
| Accumulator 1 | 4 |

###### After processing

The following table shows the contents of accumulator 1 after executing the instruction "Return remainder of division":

| Accumulator | Value |
| --- | --- |
| Accumulator 1 | 1 |

---

#### Floating-point numbers (S7-300, S7-400)

This section contains information on the following topics:

- [+R: Add floating-point numbers (S7-300, S7-400)](#r-add-floating-point-numbers-s7-300-s7-400)
- [-R: Subtract floating-point numbers (S7-300, S7-400)](#r-subtract-floating-point-numbers-s7-300-s7-400)
- [*R: Multiply floating-point numbers (S7-300, S7-400)](#r-multiply-floating-point-numbers-s7-300-s7-400)
- [/R: Divide floating-point numbers (S7-300, S7-400)](#r-divide-floating-point-numbers-s7-300-s7-400)
- [ABS: Form absolute value (S7-300, S7-400)](#abs-form-absolute-value-s7-300-s7-400)

##### +R: Add floating-point numbers (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Add floating-point numbers" instruction to add the values contained in accumulators 1 and 2. The instruction interprets these values as floating-point numbers. The instruction saves the sum in accumulator 1.

After the instruction has executed, the status bits CC 0 and CC 1 indicate whether the sum is negative, zero or positive. If the number is outside the permitted number range, the status bits OV and OS are set to "1".

If an invalid floating-point number or the sign for infinity (+/- ∞) is entered, the instruction writes an invalid value to accumulator 1 and sets the status bits CC 0, CC 1, OV and OS to "1".

In case of controllers with two accumulators the content of accumulator 2 remains unchanged after processing of the instruction.

In case of controllers with four accumulators the contents of accumulator 3 are copied to accumulator 2 and the contents of accumulator 4 are copied to accumulator 3. The contents of accumulator 4 remain unchanged after the instruction has executed.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load first value for addition. |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Load second value for addition. |
| +R | // Add values |
| T "Tag_Result" | // Transfer sum to the operand "Tag_Result". |

---

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)

##### -R: Subtract floating-point numbers (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

With the "Subtract floating-point numbers" instruction you subtract the value of accumulator 1 from the value of accumulator 2. The instruction interprets the values of accumulators 1 and 2 as floating-point numbers. The instruction stores the difference in accumulator 1.

After the instruction has executed, the status bits CC 0 and CC 1 indicate whether the difference is negative, zero or positive. If the number is outside the permitted number range, the status bits OV and OS are set to "1".

If an invalid floating-point number or the sign for infinity (+/- ∞) is entered, the instruction writes an invalid value to accumulator 1 and sets the status bits CC 0, CC 1, OV and OS to "1".

In case of controllers with two accumulators the content of accumulator 2 remains unchanged after processing of the instruction.

In case of controllers with four accumulators the contents of accumulator 3 are copied to accumulator 2 and the contents of accumulator 4 are copied to accumulator 3. The contents of accumulator 4 remain unchanged after the instruction has executed.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load first value of subtraction into accumulator 1. |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Shift the contents of accumulator 1 to accumulator 2.  // Load the second value of subtraction into accumulator 1. |
| -R | // Subtract value of accumulator 1 from value of accumulator 2. |
| T "Tag_Result" | // Transfer difference to the operand "Tag_Result". |

---

##### *R: Multiply floating-point numbers (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Multiply floating-point numbers" instruction to multiply the values contained in accumulators 1 and 2. The instruction interprets these values as floating-point numbers. The instruction saves the product in accumulator 1.

After the instruction has executed, the status bits CC 0 and CC 1 indicate whether the product is negative, zero or positive. If the number is outside the permitted number range, the status bits OV and OS are set to "1".

If an invalid floating-point number or the sign for infinity (+/- ∞) is entered, the instruction writes an invalid value to accumulator 1 and sets the status bits CC 0, CC 1, OV and OS to "1".

In case of controllers with two accumulators the content of accumulator 2 remains unchanged after processing of the instruction.

In case of controllers with four accumulators the contents of accumulator 3 are copied to accumulator 2 and the contents of accumulator 4 are copied to accumulator 3. The contents of accumulator 4 remain unchanged after the instruction has executed.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load first value for multiplication. |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Load second value for multiplication. |
| *R | // Multiply values |
| T "Tag_Result" | // Transfer product to the operand "Tag_Result". |

---

##### /R: Divide floating-point numbers (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

With the "Divide floating-point numbers" instruction you divide the value of accumulator 2 by the value of accumulator 1. The instruction interprets the values of accumulators 1 and 2 as floating-point numbers. The instruction saves the result of the division (quotient) in accumulator 1.

After the instruction has executed, the status bits CC 0 and CC 1 indicate whether the quotient is negative, zero or positive. If the number is outside the permitted number range, the status bits OV and OS are set to "1".

In the case of a division by zero, the instruction reports the value zero as quotient. In this case, status bits CC 0, CC 1, OV and OS are set to signal state "1".

If an invalid floating-point number or the sign for infinity (+/- ∞) is entered, the instruction writes an invalid value to accumulator 1 and sets the status bits CC 0, CC 1, OV and OS to "1".

In case of controllers with two accumulators the content of accumulator 2 remains unchanged after processing of the instruction.

In case of controllers with four accumulators the contents of accumulator 3 are copied to accumulator 2 and the contents of accumulator 4 are copied to accumulator 3. The contents of accumulator 4 remain unchanged after the instruction has executed.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load dividend in accumulator 1. |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Move dividend to accumulator 2.  // Load divisor in accumulator 1. |
| /R | // Divide the value of accumulator 2 by the value of accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Result" | // Transfer quotients to the operand "Tag_Result". |

---

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)

[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

##### ABS: Form absolute value (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Form absolute value" instruction to form the absolute value of the value in accumulator 1. The instruction interprets the contents of accumulator 1 as a floating-point number and sets the sign of the mantissa to "0". The result is stored in accumulator 1.

The "Form absolute value" instruction does not affect any status bits.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value" | // Load floating-point number into accumulator 1 |
| ABS | // Form absolute value |
| T "Tag_Result" | // Transfer the result to operand "Tag_Result". |

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Operand | Value |
| --- | --- |
| Tag_Value | `-1.5E+02` |
| Tag_Result | `1.5E+02` |

---

#### Advanced floating-point numbers (S7-300, S7-400)

This section contains information on the following topics:

- [SQR: Form square (S7-300, S7-400)](#sqr-form-square-s7-300-s7-400)
- [SQRT: Form square root (S7-300, S7-400)](#sqrt-form-square-root-s7-300-s7-400)
- [EXP: Form exponential value (S7-300, S7-400)](#exp-form-exponential-value-s7-300-s7-400)
- [LN: Form natural logarithm (S7-300, S7-400)](#ln-form-natural-logarithm-s7-300-s7-400)
- [SIN: Form sine value (S7-300, S7-400)](#sin-form-sine-value-s7-300-s7-400)
- [ASIN: Form arcsine value (S7-300, S7-400)](#asin-form-arcsine-value-s7-300-s7-400)
- [COS: Form cosine value (S7-300, S7-400)](#cos-form-cosine-value-s7-300-s7-400)
- [ACOS: Form arccosine value (S7-300, S7-400)](#acos-form-arccosine-value-s7-300-s7-400)

##### SQR: Form square (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Form square" instruction to calculate the square of a floating-point number located in accumulator 1. The result is stored in accumulator 1.

After the instruction has executed, the status bits CC 0 and CC 1 indicate whether the result is negative, zero or positive. If the number is outside the permitted number range, the status bits OV and OS are set to "1".

If the floating-point numbers are invalid, the instruction sets the status bits CC 0, CC 1, OV and OS to "1".

The instruction influences only the contents of accumulator 1. The contents of the other accumulators remain unchanged.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_1" in accumulator 1 |
| SQR | // Form square  // Store result in accumulator 1. |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Shift the contents of accumulator 1 to accumulator 2.  // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_2" in accumulator 1 |
| *R | // Multiply the values of accumulator 1 and 2.  // Store product in accumulator 1. |

---

##### SQRT: Form square root (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Form square root" instruction to form the square root of the floating-point number located in accumulator 1. The result is stored in accumulator 1.

After the instruction has executed, the status bits CC 0 and CC 1 indicate whether the result is negative, zero or positive. If the number is outside the permitted number range, the status bits OV and OS are set to "1".

If accumulator 1 has a value less than zero or an invalid floating-point number, the instruction writes an invalid value to accumulator 1 and sets the status bits CC 0, CC 1, OV and OS to "1".

If accumulator 1 has the value "0", the instruction returns the value "0".

The instruction influences only the contents of accumulator 1. The contents of the other accumulators remain unchanged.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_1" in accumulator 1 |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Shift the contents of accumulator 1 to accumulator 2.  // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_2" in accumulator 1 |
| +R | // Add the values of accumulator 1 and 2.  // Store sum in accumulator 1. |
| SQRT | // Get square root |
| T "Tag_Result" | // Transfer result (contents of accumulator 1) to the operand "Tag_Result". |

---

##### EXP: Form exponential value (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Form exponential value" to form the exponent from the base e (e = 2.718282) and the floating-point number in accumulator 1. The instruction stores the result in accumulator 1.

After the instruction has executed, the status bits CC 0 and CC 1 indicate whether the result is negative, zero or positive. If the number is outside the permitted number range, the status bits OV and OS are set to "1".

If the floating-point numbers are invalid, the instruction sets the status bits CC 0, CC 1, OV and OS to "1".

The instruction influences only the contents of accumulator 1. The contents of the other accumulators remain unchanged.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_1" in accumulator 1 |
| EXP | // Form exponential value  // Store result in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Result" | // Transfer result (contents of accumulator 1) to the operand "Tag_Result". |

---

[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

##### LN: Form natural logarithm (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Form natural logarithm" instruction to calculate the natural logarithm of the value in accumulator 1 to base e (e = 2.718282).

After the instruction has executed, the status bits CC 0 and CC 1 indicate whether the result is negative, zero or positive. If the number is outside the permitted number range, the status bits OV and OS are set to "1".

If accumulator 1 has a value less than or equal to zero, the instruction writes an invalid value to accumulator 1 and sets the status bits CC 0, CC 1, OV and OS to "1". If the floating-point numbers are invalid, the instruction also sets the status bits CC 0, CC 1, OV and OS to "1".

The instruction influences only the contents of accumulator 1. The contents of the other accumulators remain unchanged.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_1" in accumulator 1 |
| LN | // Form natural logarithm  // Store result in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Result" | // Transfer result (contents of accumulator 1) to the operand "Tag_Result". |

---

[Inserting STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#inserting-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

##### SIN: Form sine value (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Form sine value" instruction to calculate the sine of the angle in accumulator 1. The angle must be specified in radian measure and exist as floating-point number in accumulator 1. The instruction stores the result in accumulator 1.

After the instruction has executed, the status bits CC 0 and CC 1 indicate whether the result is negative, zero or positive. If the number is outside the permitted number range, the status bits OV and OS are set to "1". If the floating-point numbers are invalid, the instruction sets the status bits CC 0, CC 1, OV and OS to "1".

The instruction influences only the contents of accumulator 1. The contents of the other accumulators remain unchanged.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_1" in accumulator 1 |
| SIN | // Form sine value  // Store result in accumulator 1. |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Shift the contents of accumulator 1 to accumulator 2.  // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_2" in accumulator 1 |
| *R | // Multiply the values of accumulator 1 and 2.  // Store product in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Result" | // Transfer result (contents of accumulator 1) to the operand "Tag_Result". |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)

[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

##### ASIN: Form arcsine value (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Form arcsine value" instruction to calculate the size of the angle from the value in accumulator 1 that corresponds to this value. The value of the accumulator 1 must exist as floating-point number in a value range from "-1" to "1".

The result of the instruction is returned in radian measure and stored in accumulator 1. Depending on the value of accumulator 1, the result can be in a value range from -π/2 to +π/2 (π= 3.14159).

After the instruction has executed, the status bits CC 0 and CC 1 indicate whether the result is negative, zero or positive. If the number is outside the permitted number range, the status bits OV and OS are set to "1".

If accumulator 1 has a value that exceeds the permitted value range, the instruction writes an invalid floating-point number to accumulator 1 and sets the status bits CC 0, CC 1, OV and OS to "1". If the floating-point numbers are invalid, the instruction also sets the status bits CC 0, CC 1, OV and OS to "1".

The instruction influences only the contents of accumulator 1. The contents of the other accumulators remain unchanged.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_1" in accumulator 1 |
| ASIN | // Form arcsine value  // Store result in accumulator 1. |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Shift the contents of accumulator 1 to accumulator 2.  // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_2" in accumulator 1 |
| *R | // Multiply the values of accumulator 1 and 2.  // Store product in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Result" | // Transfer result (contents of accumulator 1) to the operand "Tag_Result". |

---

### Load and transfer (S7-300, S7-400)

This section contains information on the following topics:

- [Load (S7-300, S7-400)](#load-s7-300-s7-400)
- [Transfer (S7-300, S7-400)](#transfer-s7-300-s7-400)

#### Load (S7-300, S7-400)

This section contains information on the following topics:

- [L: Load (S7-300, S7-400)](#l-load-s7-300-s7-400)
- [L STW: Load status word in accumulator 1 (S7-300, S7-400)](#l-stw-load-status-word-in-accumulator-1-s7-300-s7-400)
- [LAR1: Load AR1 with contents of accumulator 1 (S7-300, S7-400)](#lar1-load-ar1-with-contents-of-accumulator-1-s7-300-s7-400)
- [LAR1 &lt;D&gt;: Load AR1 with double word or area pointer (S7-300, S7-400)](#lar1-d-load-ar1-with-double-word-or-area-pointer-s7-300-s7-400)
- [LAR1 AR2: Load AR1 with contents of AR2 (S7-300, S7-400)](#lar1-ar2-load-ar1-with-contents-of-ar2-s7-300-s7-400)
- [LAR2: Load AR2 with contents of accumulator 1 (S7-300, S7-400)](#lar2-load-ar2-with-contents-of-accumulator-1-s7-300-s7-400)
- [LAR2 &lt;D&gt;: Load AR2 with double word or area pointer (S7-300, S7-400)](#lar2-d-load-ar2-with-double-word-or-area-pointer-s7-300-s7-400)

##### L: Load (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

With the "Load" instruction you load the content of a specified operand in accumulator 1. The operand that is to be loaded can be addressed as a byte, word or double word in one of the following memory areas:

- Process image of the inputs and outputs (I, Q)
- Bit memory (M)
- Temporary local data (L)
- Data blocks (DB, DI)
- Pointer
- I/O (PI)
- Timer (T)
- Counter (C)

The memory area of accumulator 1 is organized in bytes and is 32 bits wide.

The instruction writes the content of an operand that is to be loaded in byte format right aligned in accumulator 1. The remaining Bytes in accumulator 1 are filled with "0".

The instruction writes the content of the operand to be loaded in word format to the right word of accumulator 1. The higher addressed byte is hereby transferred into the right byte (bits 0 to 7) of accumulator 1. The lower addressed byte is written to the left of it. The remaining bytes in the left word of accumulator 1 are filled with "0".

The instruction writes the content of the operand to be loaded in double word format to the 32 bits of accumulator 1. The highest addressed byte is hereby transferred into the right byte (bits 0 to 7) of accumulator 1. The lowest addressed byte is written in bits 24 to 31.

The following table shows, as an example, how the contents of accumulator 1 are changed by the loading of operands in byte, word and double word format:

| Instruction | Accumulator 1 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | 31 . . . | . . . 24 | 23 . . . | . . . 16 | 15 . . . | . . . 8 | 7 . . . | . . . 0 |
| Loading of a byte: L MB10 | 0000 | 0000 | 0000 | 0000 | 0000 | 0000 | &lt;MB10&gt; |  |
| Loading of a word: L MW10 | 0000 | 0000 | 0000 | 0000 | &lt;MB10&gt; |  | &lt;MB11&gt; |  |
| Load a double word: L MD10 | &lt;MB10&gt; |  | &lt;MB11&gt; |  | &lt;MB12&gt; |  | &lt;MB13&gt; |  |

During the loading of the specified operand the previous contents of accumulator 1 are moved to accumulator 2. The "Load" instruction transfers the complete contents of accumulator 1 to accumulator 2. The previous content of accumulator 2 is lost during this.

In case of controllers with four accumulators, the contents of accumulators 3 and 4 are not influenced by the instruction.

The CPU executes the instruction regardless of the result of logic operation and the status bit. The instruction does not affect either the result of logic operation or the status bit.

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Load" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;Operand&gt; | Input | Bit strings, integers, timers, REAL, DATE, TOD, CHAR | I, Q, PI, M, L, DB, DI, T, C, pointer, parameter | Operand whose contents are loaded. |

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_1" in accumulator 1 |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Shift the contents of accumulator 1 to accumulator 2.  // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_2" in accumulator 1 |
| *R | // Multiply the values of accumulator 1 and 2.  // Store product in accumulator 1. |
| L "Tag_Value_3" | // Shift the contents of accumulator 1 to accumulator 2.  // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_3" in accumulator 1 |
| +R | // Add the values of accumulator 1 and 2.  // Store sum in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Result" | // Transfer result (contents of accumulator 1) to the operand "Tag_Result". |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)

[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

[STL programming examples (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#stl-programming-examples-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

##### L STW: Load status word in accumulator 1 (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Load status word in accumulator 1" instruction to load the status word in accumulator 1. When it executes, the instruction writes the individual status bits in the right word of accumulator 1 The remaining bits of accumulator 1 are filled with "0".

The following table shows the contents of the accumulator after executing the "Load status word in accumulator 1" instruction:

|  | Accumulator 1 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Bit number | 31-9 | 8 | 7 | 6 | 5 | 4 | 3 | 2 | 1 | 0 |
| Content | 0 | BR | CC 1 | CC 0 | OV | OS | OR | STA | RLO | /FC |

The instruction is always executed independently of the signal state of the status bit.

> **Note**
>
> The controllers of the S7-300 series (except S7-318) do not load the status bits /FC, STA and OR into accumulator 1. These locations are written with "0".

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L STW | // Load status word in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_STW" | // Transfer the contents of accumulator 1 (status bits) to the operand "Tag_STW". |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)
  
[Address areas of the CPUs (S7-300, S7-400)](Functional%20description%20of%20S7-300-400%20CPUs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%29.md#address-areas-of-the-cpus-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[Basic information on the status word (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#basic-information-on-the-status-word-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[Inserting STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#inserting-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[Setting status bits (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-s7-300-s7-400)

##### LAR1: Load AR1 with contents of accumulator 1 (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

With the "Load AR1 with contents of accumulator 1" instruction you load address register 1 (AR1) with the contents of accumulator 1. The value of accumulator 1 must correspond to the format of a POINTER.

The CPU executes the instruction regardless of the result of logic operation and the status bit. The instruction does not affect either the result of logic operation or the status bit.

The contents of the accumulators are not changed by the instruction.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L P#10.0 | // Load pointer (P#10.0) in accumulator 1. |
| LAR1 | // Load address register 1 with contents of accumulator 1. |
| L MW [AR1,P#4.0] | // Load MW14 in accumulator 1. |
| L "Tag_Value" | // Shift the contents of accumulator 1 to accumulator 2.  // Load content of the operand "Tag_Value" in accumulator 1. |
| &gt;I | // Compare whether the value of accumulator 2 is greater than the value of accumulator 1. |
| A I [AR1,P#2.1] | // Check whether signal state of bit I12.1 is "1" and link AND with current RLO. |
| = "Tag_Output" | // If the condition is satisfied (RLO = "1"), set the operand "Tag_Output" to "1". |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)

[Basic information on the status word (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#basic-information-on-the-status-word-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[Inserting STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#inserting-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[Setting status bits (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-s7-300-s7-400)

##### LAR1 <D>: Load AR1 with double word or area pointer (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Load AR1 with double word or area pointer" instruction to load address register 1 (AR1) with the contents of a double word or an area internal or area crossing pointer. The contents of the double word must match the format of an area pointer.

The pointer and the double word can address one of the following memory areas:

- Bit memory (M)
- Temporary local data (L)
- Data blocks (DB, DI)

The CPU executes the instruction regardless of the result of logic operation and the status bit. The instruction does not affect either the result of logic operation or the status bit.

The contents of the accumulators are not changed by the instruction.

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Load AR1 with double word or area pointer" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;D&gt; | Input | DWORD, POINTER | D, M, L | Operand whose contents are loaded. |

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| LAR1 P#10.0 | // Load address register 1 with contents of the area internal pointer P#10.0. |
| L MW [AR1,P#4.0] | // Load MW14 in accumulator 1. |
| L "Tag_Value" | // Shift the contents of accumulator 1 to accumulator 2.  // Load content of the operand "Tag_Value" in accumulator 1. |
| &gt;I | // Compare whether the value of accumulator 2 is greater than the value of accumulator 1. |
| A I [AR1,P#2.1] | // Check whether signal state of bit I12.1 is "1" and link AND with current RLO. |
| = "Tag_Output" | // If the condition is satisfied (RLO = "1"), set the operand "Tag_Output" to "1". |
| LAR1 MD20 | // Load address register 1 with contents of the MD20 (MD20 = P#30.0) |
| A I [AR1,P#2.1] | // Check whether signal state of bit I32.1 is "1" and link AND with current RLO. |

---

##### LAR1 AR2: Load AR1 with contents of AR2 (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Load AR1 with contents of AR2" instruction to load the contents of address register 2 (AR2) into address register 1 (AR1).

The CPU executes the instruction regardless of the result of logic operation and the status bit. The instruction does not affect either the result of logic operation or the status bit.

The contents of the accumulators are not changed by the instruction.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| LAR2 P#20.0 | // Load address register 2 with contents of the area internal pointer P#20.0. |
| LAR1 AR2 | // Copy contents of address register 2 into address register 1. |
| L MW [AR1,P#4.0] | // Load MW24 in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_2" | // Transfer accumulator 1 to "Tag_2". |

---

##### LAR2: Load AR2 with contents of accumulator 1 (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

With the "Load AR2 with contents of accumulator 1" instruction you load address register 2 (AR2) with the contents of accumulator 1. The value of accumulator 1 must correspond to the format of a POINTER.

The CPU executes the instruction regardless of the result of logic operation and the status bit. The instruction does not affect either the result of logic operation or the status bit.

The contents of the accumulators are not changed by the instruction.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L P#10.0 | // Load pointer (P#10.0) in accumulator 1. |

| L "Tag_Value" | // Shift the contents of accumulator 1 to accumulator 2.  // Load content of the operand "Tag_Value" in accumulator 1. |
| &gt;I | // Compare whether the value of accumulator 2 is greater than the value of accumulator 1. |
| A I [AR2,P#2.1] | // Check whether signal state of bit I12.1 is "1" and link AND with current RLO. |
| = "Tag_Output" | // If the condition is satisfied (RLO = "1"), set the operand "Tag_Output" to "1". |

##### LAR2 <D>: Load AR2 with double word or area pointer (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Load AR2 with double word or area pointer" instruction to load address register 2 (AR2) with the contents of a double word or an area-internal or cross-area pointer. The contents of the double word must match the format of an area pointer (POINTER).

The pointer and the double word can address one of the following memory areas:

- Bit memory (M)
- Temporary local data (L)
- Data blocks (DB, DI)

The CPU executes the instruction regardless of the result of logic operation and the status bit. The instruction does not affect either the result of logic operation or the status bit.

The contents of the accumulators are not changed by the instruction.

###### Syntax

Use the following syntax for the "Load AR2 with double word or area pointer" instruction:

LAR2 &lt;D&gt;

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Load AR2 with double word or area pointer" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;D&gt; | Input | DWORD, POINTER | D, M, L | Operand whose contents are loaded. |

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| LAR2 P#10.0 | // Load address register 2 with contents of the area internal pointer P#10.0. |
| L MW [AR2,P#4.0] | // Load MW14 in accumulator 1. |
| L "Tag_Value" | // Shift the contents of accumulator 1 to accumulator 2.  // Load content of the operand "Tag_Value" in accumulator 1. |
| &gt;I | // Compare whether the value of accumulator 2 is greater than the value of accumulator 1. |
| A I [AR2,P#2.1] | // Check whether signal state of bit I12.1 is "1" and link AND with current RLO. |
| = "Tag_Output" | // If the condition is satisfied (RLO = "1"), set the operand "Tag_Output" to "1". |
| LAR2 MD20 | // Load address register 2 with contents of the MD20 (MD20 = P#30.0) |
| A I [AR2,P#2.1] | // Check whether signal state of bit I32.1 is "1" and link AND with current RLO. |

#### Transfer (S7-300, S7-400)

This section contains information on the following topics:

- [T: Transfer (S7-300, S7-400)](#t-transfer-s7-300-s7-400)
- [T STW: Transfer accumulator 1 to status word (S7-300, S7-400)](#t-stw-transfer-accumulator-1-to-status-word-s7-300-s7-400)
- [CAR: Switch AR1 and AR2 (S7-300, S7-400)](#car-switch-ar1-and-ar2-s7-300-s7-400)
- [TAR1: Transfer AR1 to accumulator 1 (S7-300, S7-400)](#tar1-transfer-ar1-to-accumulator-1-s7-300-s7-400)
- [TAR1 &lt;D&gt;: Transfer AR1 to double word (S7-300, S7-400)](#tar1-d-transfer-ar1-to-double-word-s7-300-s7-400)
- [TAR1 AR2: Transfer AR1 to AR2 (S7-300, S7-400)](#tar1-ar2-transfer-ar1-to-ar2-s7-300-s7-400)
- [TAR2: Transfer AR2 to accumulator 1 (S7-300, S7-400)](#tar2-transfer-ar2-to-accumulator-1-s7-300-s7-400)
- [TAR2 &lt;D&gt;: Transfer AR2 to double word (S7-300, S7-400)](#tar2-d-transfer-ar2-to-double-word-s7-300-s7-400)

##### T: Transfer (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Transfer" instruction to transfer the contents of accumulator 1 in byte, word or double word format to a specified operand. The contents of accumulator 1 are not changed by this instruction. The specified operand must be addressed in one of the following memory areas:

- Process image of the inputs and outputs (I, Q)
- Bit memory (M)
- Temporary local data (L)
- Data blocks (DB, DI)
- I/O (PQ)

The number of bytes to be transferred depends on the format of the specified operand. If the operand exists in byte format, the instruction transfers the contents of the bits 0 to 7 of accumulator 1.

If the operand exists in word format, the instruction transfers the contents of the word that is right-aligned in accumulator 1. The right byte of accumulator 1 is transferred to the higher addressed byte of the operand. The bits 8 to 15 of the accumulator 1 are transferred to the lower byte of the operand.

If the specified operand exists in double word format, the instruction transfers the entire content of accumulator 1. The right byte of accumulator 1 is transferred to the highest addressed byte of the operand. The bits 24 to 31 of accumulator 1 are transferred to the lowest addressed byte of the operand.

The following table shows an example of how the contents of accumulator 1 are transferred in byte, word and double word format:

| Instruction | Accumulator 1 |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Bits | 31 . . ... . 24 | 23 . . . . . . 16 |  | 15 . . .. . . 8 | 7 . . . . . . 0 |
| Contents of accumulator 1 | byte (n) | byte (n+1) |  | byte (n+2) | byte (n+3) |
| Transfer of a byte |  |  |  |  | byte (n+3) |
| Transfer of a word |  |  |  | byte (n+2) | byte (n+3) |
| Transferring a double word | byte (n) |  | byte (n+1) | byte (n+2) | byte (n+3) |

The CPU executes the instruction regardless of the result of logic operation and the status bit. The instruction does not affect either the result of logic operation or the status bit.

The execution of the "Transfer" instruction is influenced by the Master Control Relay (MCR). When the MCR bit is set to "0", the value "0" is transferred to the specified operand.

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Transfer" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;Operand&gt; | Output | Bit strings, integers, timers, REAL, DATE, TOD, CHAR | I, Q, PQ, M, L, DB, DI | Operand to which the contents of accumulator 1 are transferred. |

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_1" in accumulator 1 |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Shift the contents of accumulator 1 to accumulator 2.  // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_2" in accumulator 1 |
| *R | // Multiply the values of accumulator 1 and 2.  // Store product in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Result_1" | // Transfer product (contents of Accumulator 1) to the operand "Tag_Result_1". |
| L "Tag_Value_3" | // Shift the contents of accumulator 1 to accumulator 2.  // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_3" in accumulator 1 |
| +R | // Add the values of accumulator 1 and 2.  // Store sum in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Result_2" | // Transfer sum (contents of Accumulator 1) to the operand "Tag_Result_2" |

---

##### T STW: Transfer accumulator 1 to status word (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Transfer accumulator 1 to status word" instruction to transfer bits 0 to 8 of accumulator 1 to the status word.

The following table shows the bits in accumulator 1 that will overwrite status bits with processing of the instruction:

|  | Accumulator 1 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Bit number | 8 | 7 | 6 | 5 | 4 | 3 | 2 | 1 | 0 |
| Status bits | BR | CC 1 | CC 0 | OV | OS | OR | STA | RLO | /FC |

The instruction is always executed independently of the signal state of the status bit.

> **Note**
>
> The bits of the status word /FC, STA and OR are not loaded by the "Transfer accumulator 1 to status word" instruction. Only bits 1, 4, 5, 6, 7 and 8 are loaded to the corresponding bit positions of the lower value word of accumulator 1.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_STW" | // Load value of the operand "Tag_STW" in accumulator 1. |
| T STW | // Transfer bits 0 to 8 of accumulator 1 to status word |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)
  
[Address areas of the CPUs (S7-300, S7-400)](Functional%20description%20of%20S7-300-400%20CPUs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%29.md#address-areas-of-the-cpus-s7-300-s7-400)

[Setting status bits (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-s7-300-s7-400)

##### CAR: Switch AR1 and AR2 (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the instruction "Switch AR1 and AR2" to switch the contents of address registers 1 (AR1) and 2 (AR2).

The CPU executes the instruction regardless of the result of logic operation and the status bit. The instruction does not affect either the result of logic operation or the status bit.

The contents of the accumulators are not changed by the instruction.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| LAR1 P#10.0 | // Load address register 1 with contents of the area internal pointer P#10.0. |
| LAR2 P#20.0 | // Load address register 2 with contents of the area internal pointer P#20.0. |
| CAR | // Switch contents of the address registers. |
| L MD [AR1,P#2.0] | // Load MD22 in accumulator 1. |
| T MD [AR2,P#2.0] | // Transfer MD12 too accumulator 2. |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)
  
[Address areas of the CPUs (S7-300, S7-400)](Functional%20description%20of%20S7-300-400%20CPUs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%29.md#address-areas-of-the-cpus-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[Basic information on the status word (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#basic-information-on-the-status-word-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[Inserting STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#inserting-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[Setting status bits (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-s7-300-s7-400)

##### TAR1: Transfer AR1 to accumulator 1 (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

With the "Transfer AR1 to accumulator 1" instruction you transfer the contents of address register 1 (AR1) to accumulator 1. The content of accumulator 1 is moved to accumulator 2 during this.

The CPU executes the instruction regardless of the result of logic operation and the status bit. The instruction does not affect either the result of logic operation or the status bit.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| LAR1 P#15.0 | // Load contents of the area-internal pointer P#15.0 into address register 1. |
| TAR1 | // Transfer contents of address register 1 (P#15.0) to accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Pointer" | // Transfer contents of accumulator 1 to the operand "Tag_Pointer". |

---

**See also**

[Setting status bits (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-s7-300-s7-400)

##### TAR1 <D>: Transfer AR1 to double word (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Transfer AR1 to double word" instruction to transfer the contents of address register 1 (AR1) to a double word. The double word must hereby be addressed in one of the following memory areas:

- Bit memory (M)
- Temporary local data (L)
- Data blocks (DB, DI)

The CPU executes the instruction regardless of the result of logic operation and the status bit. The instruction does not affect either the result of logic operation or the status bit.

The contents of the accumulators are not changed by the instruction.

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Transfer AR1 to double word" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;D&gt; | Output | DWORD | D, M, L | Operand to which the contents of accumulator 1 are transferred. |

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| TAR1 %DBD20 | // Transfer contents of address register 1 to data double word DBD20. |
| TAR1 %DID30 | // Transfer contents of address register 1 to instance double word DID30. |
| TAR1 %LD18 | // Transfer contents of address register 1 to local data double word LD18. |
| TAR1 %MD24 | // Transfer contents of address register 1 to memory double word MD24. |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)
  
[Address areas of the CPUs (S7-300, S7-400)](Functional%20description%20of%20S7-300-400%20CPUs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%29.md#address-areas-of-the-cpus-s7-300-s7-400)

[Setting status bits (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-s7-300-s7-400)

##### TAR1 AR2: Transfer AR1 to AR2 (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Transfer AR1 to AR2" instruction to copy the contents of address register 1 (AR1) to address register 2 (AR2).

The CPU executes the instruction regardless of the result of logic operation and the status bit. The instruction does not affect either the result of logic operation or the status bit.

The contents of the accumulators are not changed by the instruction.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| LAR1 P#10.4 | // Load contents of the area-internal pointer P#10.4 into address register 1. |
| TAR1 AR2 | // Transfer contents of address register 1 to address register 2. |
| A I [AR2,P#3.2] | // Check whether signal state of bit I13.6 is "1" and AND with current RLO. |
| = "Tag1" | // Set operand "Tag_1" to "1" |

---

**See also**

##### TAR2: Transfer AR2 to accumulator 1 (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

With the "Transfer AR2 to accumulator 1" instruction you transfer the contents of address register 2 (AR2) to accumulator 1. The content of accumulator 1 is moved to accumulator 2 during this.

The CPU executes the instruction regardless of the result of logic operation and the status bit. The instruction does not affect either the result of logic operation or the status bit.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| LAR2 P#20.0 | // Load address register 2 with contents of the area internal pointer P#20.0. |
| TAR2 | // Transfer contents of address register 2 (P#20.0) to accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Pointer" | // Transfer contents of accumulator 1 to the operand "Tag_Pointer". |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)

###### Description

Use the "Transfer AR2 to double word" instruction to transfer the contents of address register 2 (AR2) to a double word. The double word must hereby be addressed in one of the following memory areas:

The CPU executes the instruction regardless of the result of logic operation and the status bit. The instruction does not affect either the result of logic operation or the status bit.

This section contains information on the following topics:

- [DTB: Convert integer (32 bit) to BCD (S7-300, S7-400)](#dtb-convert-integer-32-bit-to-bcd-s7-300-s7-400)

- [INVD: Create ones complement double integer (32 bit) (S7-300, S7-400)](#invd-create-ones-complement-double-integer-32-bit-s7-300-s7-400)
- [NEGI: Negate integer (16 bit) (S7-300, S7-400)](#negi-negate-integer-16-bit-s7-300-s7-400)
