- [NEGR: Negate floating-point number (S7-300, S7-400)](#negr-negate-floating-point-number-s7-300-s7-400)
- [CAW: Switch bytes in the right word of accumulator 1 (S7-300, S7-400)](#caw-switch-bytes-in-the-right-word-of-accumulator-1-s7-300-s7-400)
- [CAD: Switch all bytes in accumulator 1 (S7-300, S7-400)](#cad-switch-all-bytes-in-accumulator-1-s7-300-s7-400)
- [RND: Round numerical value (S7-300, S7-400)](#rnd-round-numerical-value-s7-300-s7-400)
- [TRUNC: Truncate numerical value (S7-300, S7-400)](#trunc-truncate-numerical-value-s7-300-s7-400)
- [RND+: Generate next higher integer from floating-point number (S7-300, S7-400)](#rnd-generate-next-higher-integer-from-floating-point-number-s7-300-s7-400)
- [RND-: Generate next lower integer from floating-point number (S7-300, S7-400)](#rnd--generate-next-lower-integer-from-floating-point-number-s7-300-s7-400)

#### BTI: Convert BCD to integer (16 bit) (S7-300, S7-400)

##### Description

Use the "Convert BCD to integer (16 bit)" instruction to convert the value in the right word of accumulator 1 to a 16-bit integer. The instruction interprets the word that is to be converted as a three-digit binary coded decimal (BCD).

The bits 1 to 11 of accumulator 1 indicate the value that will be converted. Values in the range from "-999" to "+999" are permitted.

The sign of the result value is read from bit 15 of accumulator 1. If the signal state of the bit is "0", the sign is positive. If the signal state of the bit is "1," the sign is negative. Bits 12 through 14 are not used in the conversion.

If the BCD code contains a pseudo tetrad, the CPU reports a programming error and opens the organization block "OB121". If the organization block OB121 is not present, the CPU changes to STOP mode.

The result of the conversion is saved in the right word of accumulator 1. The contents of the left word in accumulator 1 are not affected by the instruction.

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Input" | // Load BCD in accumulator 1. |
| BTI | // Convert BCD to 16-bit integer. |
| T "Tag_Output" | // Transfer the result to operand "Tag_Output". |

The following figure shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

![Example](images/44984884107_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

#### ITB: Convert integer (16 bit) to BCD (S7-300, S7-400)

##### Description

Use the "Convert integer (16 bit) to BCD" instruction to convert the value in the right word of accumulator 1 to a three-digit binary-coded decimal (BCD). The instruction interprets the value that is to be converted as a 16-bit integer.

The bits 0 to 11 of accumulator 1 indicate the value that will be converted. Values in the range from "-999" to "+999" are permitted. If the value to be converted is outside this range, the bits OV and OS are set to signal state "1". In this case the conversion is not executed.

The sign of the result value is read from bits 12 through 15 of accumulator 1. If the signal state of the bits is "0", the sign is positive. If the signal state of all four bits is "1", the sign is negative.

The result of the conversion is saved in the right word of accumulator 1. The contents of the left word in accumulator 1 are not affected by the instruction.

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Input" | // Load integer (16 bit) in accumulator 1. |
| ITB | // Convert integer to BCD. |
| T "Tag_Output" | // Transfer the result to operand "Tag_Output". |

The following figure shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

![Example](images/44985237259_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

#### BTD: Convert BCD to integer (32 bit) (S7-300, S7-400)

##### Description

Use the "Convert BCD to integer (32 bit)" to convert the value in accumulator 1 to a 32-bit integer. The instruction interprets the value that is to be converted as a seven-digit binary coded binary coded decimal (BCD).

The bits 0 to 27 of accumulator 1 indicate the value that will be converted. Values in the range from "-9999999" through "+9999999" are permitted.

The sign of the result value is read from bit 31 of accumulator 1. If the signal state of the bit is "0", the sign is positive. If the signal state of the bit is "1," the sign is negative. Bits 28 through 30 are not used in the conversion.

The result of the instruction is saved in accumulator 1. The content of accumulator 2 remains unchanged.

If the BCD code contains a pseudo tetrad, the CPU reports a programming error and opens the organization block "OB121". If the organization block OB121 is not present, the CPU changes to stop mode.

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Input" | // Load BCD in accumulator 1. |
| BTD | // BCD is converted to 32-bit integer. |
| T "Tag_Output" | // Transfer the result to operand "Tag_Output". |

The following figure shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

![Example](images/44988892299_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

[Setting status bits (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-s7-300-s7-400)

#### ITD: Convert integer (16 bit) to integer (32 bit) (S7-300, S7-400)

##### Description

Use the "Convert integer (16 bit) to integer (32 bit)" instruction to convert the value in the right word of accumulator 1 to a 32-bit integer. The instruction interprets the value that is to be converted as a 16-bit integer.

Bits 0 through 15 are not used in the conversion. The bits 16 through 31 of the result value are filled with the signal state of the bit 15.

The result value is saved in accumulator 1. The content of accumulator 2 remains unchanged.

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Input" | // Load integer (16 bit) in accumulator 1. |
| ITD | // Convert integer (16 bit) to integer (32 bit). |
| T "Tag_Output" | // Transfer the result to operand "Tag_Output". |

The following table shows the contents of accumulator 1 before and after processing of the instruction:

| Status | Accumulator 1 |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | 31 . . . | . . . . | . . . . | . . . 16 | 15 . . . | . . . . | . . . . | . . . 0 |
| Before processing | XXXX | XXXX | XXXX | XXXX | 1111 | 1111 | 1111 | 0110 |
| After processing | 1111 | 1111 | 1111 | 1111 | 1111 | 1111 | 1111 | 0110 |
|  | X: The signal state of the bits is irrelevant for the conversion |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)
  
[Address areas of the CPUs (S7-300, S7-400)](Functional%20description%20of%20S7-300-400%20CPUs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%29.md#address-areas-of-the-cpus-s7-300-s7-400)

[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

#### DTB: Convert integer (32 bit) to BCD (S7-300, S7-400)

##### Description

Use the "Convert integer (32 bit) to BCD" instruction to convert the value in accumulator 1 to a seven-digit binary coded decimal (BCD). The instruction interprets the value that is to be converted as a 32-bit integer.

The bits 0 to 27 of accumulator 1 indicate the value that will be converted. Values in the range from "-9999999" through "+9999999" are permitted. If the value to be converted is outside this range, the bits OV and OS are set to signal state "1". In this case the conversion is not executed.

The sign of the result value is read from bits 28 through 31 of accumulator 1. If the signal state of the bits is "0", the sign is positive. If the signal state of all four bits is "1", the sign is negative.

The result of the instruction is saved in accumulator 1. The content of accumulator 2 remains unchanged.

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Input" | // Load integer (32 bit) to accumulator 1 |
| DTB | // Convert integer (32 bit) to BCD |
| T "Tag_Output" | // Transfer the result to operand "Tag_Output". |

#### DTR: Convert integer (32 bit) to floating-point number (S7-300, S7-400)

##### Description

Use the "Convert integer (32 bit) to floating-point number" instruction to convert the value in accumulator 1 to a floating-point number. The instruction interprets the value that is to be converted as a 32-bit integer.

Because a 32-bit integer has a higher accuracy than a floating-point number, the result of the conversion is rounded off to the next integer.

The result of the instruction is saved in accumulator 1. The content of accumulator 2 remains unchanged.

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Input" | // Load integer (32 bit) to accumulator 1 |
| DTR | // Convert integer (32 bit) to floating-point number. |
| T "Tag_Output" | // Transfer the result to operand "Tag_Output". |

The following figure shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

![Example](images/44990292235_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[Setting status bits (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-s7-300-s7-400)

#### INVI: Create ones complement integer (16 bit) (S7-300, S7-400)

##### Description

Use the "Create ones complement integer (16 bit)" instruction to negate the value in the right word of accumulator 1 bit for bit.

When executed, the instruction inverts the signal state of each individual bit in the right word of accumulator 1. The ones are replaced with zeros and the zeros with ones.

The result is saved in the right word of accumulator 1. The contents of the left word in accumulator 1 are not affected by the instruction.

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Input" | // Load value in accumulator 1 |
| INVI | // Create ones complement |
| T "Tag_Output" | // Transfer the result to operand "Tag_Output". |

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Operand | Value |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | 15 . . . | . . . . | . . . . | . . . 0 |
| Tag_Input | 0110 | 0011 | 1010 | 1110 |
| Tag_Output | 1001 | 1100 | 0101 | 0001 |

---

[Setting status bits (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-s7-300-s7-400)

#### INVD: Create ones complement double integer (32 bit) (S7-300, S7-400)

##### Description

Use the "Create ones complement double integer (32 bit)" to negate the value in accumulator 1 bit for bit.

During execution, the instruction inverts the signal state of each individual bit in accumulator 1. The ones are replaced with zeros and the zeros with ones.

The result of the instruction is saved in accumulator 1. The content of accumulator 2 remains unchanged.

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Input" | // Load value in accumulator 1 |
| INVD | // Create ones complement |
| T "Tag_Output" | // Transfer the result to operand "Tag_Output". |

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Operand | Value |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | 31 . . . | . . . . | . . . . | . . . 16 | 15 . . . | . . . . | . . . . | . . . 0 |
| Tag_Input | 0110 | 1111 | 1000 | 1100 | 0110 | 0011 | 1010 | 1110 |
| Tag_Output | 1001 | 0000 | 0111 | 0011 | 1001 | 1100 | 0101 | 0001 |

#### NEGI: Negate integer (16 bit) (S7-300, S7-400)

##### Description

Use the "Negate integer (16 bit)" instruction to change the sign of the value in the right word of accumulator 1 by forming the twos complement. The instruction interprets the value of accumulator 1 as a 16-bit integer.

The processing of the instruction is equal to a multiplication with "-1". The result of the instruction is saved in the right word of accumulator 1. The contents of the left word in accumulator 1 are not affected by the instruction.

The "Negate integer (16 bit)" instruction affects the status bits CC 0, CC 1, OV and OS. The following table shows how the instruction influences the status bit depending on the result:

| Result: | CC 1 | CC 0 | OV | OS |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| +1 to +32767 | 1 | 0 | 0 | - |
| 0 | 0 | 0 | 0 | - |
| -1 to -32767 | 0 | 1 | 0 | - |
| (-) 32768 | 0 | 1 | 1 | 1 |

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Input" | // Load value in accumulator 1 |
| NEGI | // Negate integer (16 bit) |
| T "Tag_Output" | // Transfer the result to operand "Tag_Output". |

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Operand | Value |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | 15 . . . | . . . . | . . . . | . . . 0 |
| Tag_Input | 0101 | 1101 | 0011 | 1000 |
| Tag_Output | 1010 | 0010 | 1100 | 1000 |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)
  
[Address areas of the CPUs (S7-300, S7-400)](Functional%20description%20of%20S7-300-400%20CPUs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%29.md#address-areas-of-the-cpus-s7-300-s7-400)

#### NEGD: Negate integer (32 bit) (S7-300, S7-400)

##### Description

Use the "Negate integer (32 bit)" instruction to change the sign of the value in accumulator 1 by forming the twos complement. The instruction interprets the value of accumulator 1 as a 32-bit integer.

The processing of the instruction is equal to a multiplication with "-1". The result of the instruction is saved in accumulator 1. The content of accumulator 2 remains unchanged.

The "Negate integer (32 bit)" instruction affects the status bits CC 0, CC 1, OV and OS. The following table shows how the instruction influences the status bit depending on the result:

| Result | CC 1 | CC 0 | OV | OS |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| +1 to +2147483647 | 1 | 0 | 0 | - |
| 0 | 0 | 0 | 0 | - |
| -1 to -2147483647 | 0 | 1 | 0 | - |
| (-) 2147483648 | 0 | 1 | 1 | 1 |

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Input" | // Load value in accumulator 1 |
| NEGD | // Negate integer (32 bit). |
| T "Tag_Output" | // Transfer the result to operand "Tag_Output". |

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Status | Value |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | 31 . . . | . . . . | . . . . | . . . 16 | 15 . . . | . . . . | . . . . | . . . 0 |
| Tag_Input | 0101 | 1111 | 0110 | 0100 | 0101 | 1101 | 0011 | 1000 |
| Tag_Output | 1010 | 0000 | 1001 | 1011 | 1010 | 0010 | 1100 | 1000 |

#### NEGR: Negate floating-point number (S7-300, S7-400)

##### Description

With the "Negate floating-point number" instruction you invert the signal state of bit 31 in accumulator 1. The instruction interprets the value of accumulator 1 as a floating-point number. The sign of the mantissa is in bit 31 of the floating-point number.

The processing of the instruction is equal to a multiplication with "-1". After the processing of the instruction, the sign of the mantissa is inverted.

The result of the instruction is saved in accumulator 1. The content of accumulator 2 remains unchanged.

The instruction does not affect any status bits.

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Input" | // Load floating-point number into accumulator 1 |
| NEGR | // Negate floating-point number. |
| T "Tag_Output" | // Transfer the result to operand "Tag_Output". |

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Operand | Value |
| --- | --- |
| Tag_Input | 1.5E+02 |
| Tag_Output | -1.5E+02 |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)
  
[Address areas of the CPUs (S7-300, S7-400)](Functional%20description%20of%20S7-300-400%20CPUs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%29.md#address-areas-of-the-cpus-s7-300-s7-400)

[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

#### CAW: Switch bytes in the right word of accumulator 1 (S7-300, S7-400)

##### Description

Use the "Switch bytes in the right word of accumulator 1" instruction to switch the sequence of the two right bytes in the right word of accumulator 1.

The following table shows the contents of accumulator 1 before and after processing of the instruction:

| Status | Bytes in accumulator 1 |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Before processing | Value A | Value B | Value C | Value D |
| After processing | Value A | Value B | Value D | Value C |

The result of the instruction is saved in the right word of accumulator 1. The bytes in the left word of accumulator 1 are not influenced by the instruction and remain unchanged.

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Input" | // Load value in accumulator. |
| CAW | // Switch bytes in the right word of accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Output" | // Transfer the result to operand "Tag_Output". |

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Operand | Value |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Tag_Input | 0000 | 1111 | 0000 | 1111 |
| Tag_Output | 0000 | 1111 | 1111 | 0000 |

---

#### CAD: Switch all bytes in accumulator 1 (S7-300, S7-400)

##### Description

Use the "Switch all bytes in accumulator 1" instruction to switch the sequence of the bytes in accumulator 1.

The following table shows the contents of accumulator 1 before and after processing of the instruction:

| Status | Bytes in accumulator 1 |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Before processing | Value A | Value B | Value C | Value D |
| After processing | Value D | Value C | Value B | Value A |

The result of the instruction is saved in accumulator 1. The content of accumulator 2 remains unchanged.

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Input" | // Load value of the operand in accumulator 1. |
| CAD | // Switch bytes of accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Output" | // Transfer the result to operand "Tag_Output". |

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Operand | Value |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Tag_Input | 1111 | 0000 | 0000 | 1111 | 0000 | 0000 | 1111 | 1111 |
| Tag_Output | 1111 | 1111 | 0000 | 0000 | 0000 | 1111 | 1111 | 0000 |

[Setting status bits (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-s7-300-s7-400)

#### RND: Round numerical value (S7-300, S7-400)

##### Description

Use the "Round numerical value" instruction to convert the value in accumulator 1 to a 32-bit integer. The instruction interprets the value that is to be converted as a floating-point number and round this to the next integer.

If the floating-point number is exactly between an even and odd number, the even number is selected as result.

The result of the instruction is saved in accumulator 1. The content of accumulator 2 remains unchanged.

The conversion is not executed and the status bits OV and OS are set, if one of the following conditions applies:

- The value in accumulator 1 is not a valid floating-point number.
- The result is outside the range permitted for an integer of the data type DINT.

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Input" | // Load floating-point number into accumulator 1 |
| RND | // Round floating-point number to an integer. |
| T "Tag_Output" | // Transfer the result to operand "Tag_Output". |

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Operand | Values |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Tag_Input | 101.5 | -101.5 |
| Tag_Output | 102 | -102 |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)

[Basic information on the status word (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#basic-information-on-the-status-word-s7-300-s7-400)

[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

#### TRUNC: Truncate numerical value (S7-300, S7-400)

##### Description

Use the "Truncate numerical value" instruction to convert the value in accumulator 1 to a 32-bit integer. The instruction interprets the value to be converted as a floating-point number and returns its whole number as result.

The result of the instruction is saved in accumulator 1. The content of accumulator 2 remains unchanged.

The conversion is not executed and the status bits OV and OS are set, if one of the following conditions applies:

- The value in accumulator 1 is not a valid floating-point number.
- The result is outside the range permitted for an integer of the data type DINT.

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Input" | // Load floating-point number into accumulator 1 |
| TRUNC | // Convert floating-point number to an integer of data type DINT. |
| T "Tag_Output" | // Transfer the result to operand "Tag_Output". |

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Operand | Values |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Tag_Input | 101.5 | -101.5 |
| Tag_Output | 101 | -101 |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)

[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

#### RND+: Generate next higher integer from floating-point number (S7-300, S7-400)

##### Description

Use the "Generate next higher integer from floating-point number" instruction to convert the value in accumulator 1 to a 32-bit integer. The instruction interprets the value that is to be converted as a floating-point number and rounds this number to the next higher integer. The result of the instruction is a number of the data type DINT that is greater than or equal to the floating-point number to be converted.

The result of the instruction is saved in accumulator 1. The content of accumulator 2 remains unchanged.

The conversion is not executed and the status bits OV and OS are set, if one of the following conditions applies:

- The value in accumulator 1 is not a valid floating-point number.
- The result is outside the range permitted for an integer of the data type DINT.

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Input" | // Load floating-point number into accumulator 1 |
| RND+ | // Round floating-point number to next higher integer. |
| T "Tag_Output" | // Transfer the result to operand "Tag_Output". |

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Operand | Values |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Tag_Input | 100.5 | -100.5 |
| Tag_Output | 101 | -100 |

---

**See also**

[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

#### RND-: Generate next lower integer from floating-point number (S7-300, S7-400)

##### Description

Use the "Generate next lower integer from floating-point number" instruction to convert the value in accumulator 1 to a 32-bit integer. The instruction interprets the value that is to be converted as a floating-point number and rounds this number to the next lower integer. The result of the instruction is a number of the data type DINT that is less than or equal to the floating-point number to be converted.

The result of the instruction is saved in accumulator 1. The content of accumulator 2 remains unchanged.

The conversion is not executed and the status bits OV and OS are set, if one of the following conditions applies:

- The value in accumulator 1 is not a valid floating-point number.
- The result is outside the range permitted for an integer of the data type DINT.

##### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Input" | // Load floating-point number into accumulator 1 |
| RND- | // Round floating-point number to next lower integer. |
| T "Tag_Output" | // Transfer the result to operand "Tag_Output". |

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Operand | Values |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Tag_Input | 100.5 | -100.5 |
| Tag_Output | 100 | -101 |

---

##### Jump label (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use a jump label to specify the place in the program at which the program execution should resume after a jump. The name of the jump label can consist of up to 128 letters, numbers or underscores.

The jump label and the instruction in which the jump label is specified must be located in the same block. The name of a jump label can only be assigned once in a block. Each jump label can jump to several locations.

Both forward and backward jumps are possible. The maximum jump distance is -32768 or +32767 words of program code. The actual maximum number of instructions you can jump over depends on the mix of the statements used in your program (one, two, or three-word instructions).

If you use the MCR functions, the jump label must be located in the same MCR range as the jump instruction.

Adhere to the following grammatical rules for jump labels:

- Letters (a to z, A to Z)
- A combination of letters and numbers. Check that the order is correct, i.e. first the letters, then the numbers (a - z, A - Z, 0 - 9).
- Special characters or a combination of letters and numbers must not be used in reverse order, i.e. first the numbers and then the letters (0-9, a - z, A - Z).

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Input_1" | // Load first comparison value. |
| L "Tag_Input_2" | // Load second comparison value. |
| &gt;I | // Check whether the value of the operand "Tag_Input_1" is greater than the value of the operand "Tag_Input_2" |
| JC MyLABEL | // With a scan result "1" jump to jump label "MyLABEL" and continue with program processing  // If the result of the query is "0", execute the next instruction. |
| L "Tag_Input_3" | // Load content of the operand "Tag_Input_3" in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Output" | // Load contents of accumulator 1 in operand "Tag_Output". |
| MyLABEL:A "Tag_Input_4" | // If there was a jump, continue program execution at this point.  // Query whether operand "Tag_Input_4" is "1" |

---

**See also**

[Basic information on the status word (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#basic-information-on-the-status-word-s7-300-s7-400)

##### JU: Unconditional jump (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Unconditional jump" instruction to interrupt the linear program execution and continue at the point that is marked by the specified jump label. The instruction is always executed independently of conditions.

The "Unconditional jump" instruction does not affect the status bits.

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Unconditional jump" instruction:

| Parameters | Description |
| --- | --- |
| &lt;jump label&gt; | Symbolic name of the jump destination |

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Input_1" | // Load first comparison value. |
| L "Tag_Input_2" | // Load second comparison value. |
| &gt;I | // Check whether the value of the operand "Tag_Input_1" is greater than the value of the operand "Tag_Input_2" |
| JC MyLABEL_1 | // With a scan result "1" jump to jump label "MyLABEL_1" and continue with program processing  // If the result of the query is "0", continue linear program execution. |
| L "Tag_Input_3" | // Load content of the operand "Tag_Input_3" in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Output_1" | // Load contents of accumulator 1 in operand "Tag_Output_1". |
| JU MyLABEL_2 | // Jump to jump label "MyLABEL_2" and resume execution of the program there. |
| MyLABEL_1: L "Tag_Input_4" | // Jump label  // Load content of the operand "Tag_Input_4" in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Output_2" | // Load contents of accumulator 1 in operand "Tag_Output_2". |
| MyLABEL_2: A "Tag_Input_5" | // Jump label "MyLABEL_2"  // Query whether operand "Tag_Input_5" is "1" |

---

**See also**

[Setting status bits in program control operation instructions (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-in-program-control-operation-instructions-s7-300-s7-400)

##### JC: Jump if RLO = 1 (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Jump if RLO = 1" instruction to interrupt linear program execution depending on the result of logic operation and resume it at the point marked by the specified jump label.

The jump to the specified jump label is only executed when the current RLO is "1". If the current RLO before the instruction is "0", the jump is not executed and the program is resumed with the next instruction.

The "Jump if RLO = 1" instruction sets the RLO and the status bit STA to "1" and the status bits OR and /FC to "0" both when the condition is met and when it is not met.

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Jump if RLO = 1" instruction:

| Parameters | Description |
| --- | --- |
| &lt;jump label&gt; | Symbolic name of the jump destination |

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Input_1" | // Load first comparison value. |
| L "Tag_Input_2" | // Load second comparison value. |
| &gt;I | // Check whether the value of the operand "Tag_Input_1" is greater than the value of the operand "Tag_Input_2" |
| JC MyLABEL | // If RLO = "1", jump to jump label "MyLABEL" and continue program execution there.  // If the RLO = "0", execute the next instruction. |
| L "Tag_Input_3" | // Load content of the operand "Tag_Input_3" in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Output_1" | // Load contents of accumulator 1 in operand "Tag_Output_1". |
| MyLABEL: L "Tag_Input_4" | // If there was a jump, continue program execution at this point.  // Load content of the operand "Tag_Input_4" in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Output_2" | // Transfer contents of accumulator 1 to the operand "Tag_Output_2". |

---

**See also**

[Setting status bits in program control operation instructions (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-in-program-control-operation-instructions-s7-300-s7-400)

##### JCN: Jump if RLO = 0 (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Jump if RLO = 0" instruction to interrupt the linear program execution depending on the result of logic operation (RLO) and resume it at the point marked by the specified jump label.

The jump to the specified jump label is only executed when the current RLO is "0". If the current RLO before the instruction is "1", the jump is not executed and the program is resumed with the next instruction.

The "Jump if RLO = 0" instruction sets the RLO and the status bit STA to "1" and the status bits OR and /FC to "0" both when the condition is met and when it is not met.

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Jump if RLO = 0" instruction:

| Parameters | Description |
| --- | --- |
| &lt;jump label&gt; | Symbolic name of the jump destination |

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| A "Tag_Input_1" | // Query whether the value of operand "Tag_Input_1" is "1" and AND. |
| A "Tag_Input_2" | // Query whether the value of operand "Tag_Input_2" is "1" and AND. |
| JCN MyLABEL | // If RLO = "0", jump to jump label "MyLABEL" and continue program execution there.  // If the RLO = "1", execute the next instruction. |
| L "Tag_Input_3" | // Load content of the operand "Tag_Input_3" in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Output" | // Load contents of accumulator 1 in operand "Tag_Output". |
| MyLABEL: A "Tag_Input_4" | // If there was a jump, continue program execution at this point.  // Query whether the value of operand "Tag_Input_4" is "1" and AND with the RLO |

---

##### JCB: Jump if RLO = 1 and save RLO (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Jump if RLO = 1 and save RLO" instruction to interrupt the linear program execution depending on the result of logic operation (RLO) and resume it at the point marked by the specified jump label. At the same time, the signal state of the current RLO is copied to the binary result (BR).

The jump to the specified jump label is only executed when the current RLO is "1". In this case the instruction set the binary result to "1".

If the current RLO before the instruction is "0", the jump is not executed and the program is resumed with the next instruction. In this case the instruction assigns the signal state "0" to the binary result.

The "Jump if RLO = 1 and save RLO" instruction sets the RLO and the status bit STA to "1" and the status bits OR and /FC to "0" both when the condition is met and when it is not met.

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Jump if RLO = 1 and save RLO" instruction:

| Parameters | Description |
| --- | --- |
| &lt;jump label&gt; | Symbolic name of the jump destination |

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Input_1" | // Load first comparison value. |
| L "Tag_Input_2" | // Load second comparison value. |
| &gt;I | // Check whether the value of the operand "Tag_Input_1" is greater than the value of the operand "Tag_Input_2" |
| JCB MyLABEL | // Copy current RLO to BR.  // If RLO = "1", jump to jump label "MyLABEL" and continue program execution there.   // If the RLO = "0", execute the next instruction. |
| L "Tag_Input_3" | // Load content of the operand "Tag_Input_3" in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Output_1" | // Load contents of accumulator 1 in operand "Tag_Output_1". |
| MyLABEL: L "Tag_Input_4" | // If there was a jump, continue program execution at this point.  // Load content of the operand "Tag_Input_4" in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Output_2" | // Load contents of accumulator 1 in operand "Tag_Output_2". |

---

**See also**

[Setting status bits in program control operation instructions (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-in-program-control-operation-instructions-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[Querying status bits with jump instructions (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#querying-status-bits-with-jump-instructions-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)

[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

##### JNB:: Jump if RLO = 0 and save RLO (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Jump if RLO = 0 and save RLO" instruction to interrupt the linear program execution depending on the result of logic operation (RLO) and resume it at the point marked by the specified jump label. At the same time, the signal state of the current result of logic operation is copied to the binary result (BR).

The jump to the specified jump label is only executed when the current RLO is "0". In this case the instruction sets the binary result to "0".

If the current RLO before the instruction is "1", the jump is not executed and the program is resumed with the next instruction. In this case the instruction assigns the signal state "1" to the binary result.

The "Jump if RLO = 0 and save RLO" instruction sets the RLO and the status bit STA to "1" and the status bits OR and /FC to "0" both when the condition is met and when it is not met.

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Jump if RLO = 0 and save RLO" instruction:

| Parameters | Description |
| --- | --- |
| &lt;jump label&gt; | Symbolic name of the jump destination |

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| A "Tag_Input_1" | // Query whether the value of operand "Tag_Input_1" is "1" and AND. |
| A "Tag_Input_2" | // Query whether the value of operand "Tag_Input_2" is "1" and AND. |
| JNB MyLABEL | // Copy current RLO to BR.  // If RLO = "0", jump to jump label "MyLABEL" and continue program execution there.  // If the RLO = "1", execute the next instruction. |
| L "Tag_Input_3" | // Load content of the operand "Tag_Input_3" in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Output" | // Transfer contents of accumulator 1 to the operand "Tag_Output". |
| MyLABEL: A "Tag_Input_4" | // If there was a jump, continue program execution at this point.  // Query whether the value of operand "Tag_Input_4" is "1" and AND with the RLO |

---

**See also**

[Setting status bits in program control operation instructions (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-in-program-control-operation-instructions-s7-300-s7-400)

[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

##### JBI: Jump if BR = 1 (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Jump if BR = 1" instruction to interrupt linear program execution depending on the binary result and resume it at the point marked by the specified jump label.

The jump to the specified jump label is only executed if the status bit BR is "1". If the status bit BR is "0", the jump is not executed and the program resumes with the next instruction.

The "Jump if BR = 1" instruction sets the status bit STA to "1" and the status bits OR and /FC to "0" both when the condition is met and when it is not met.

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Jump if BR = 1" instruction:

| Parameters | Description |
| --- | --- |
| &lt;jump label&gt; | Symbolic name of the jump destination |

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| SET | // Set RLO at the start of block to "1" |
| SAVE | // Transfer signal state of the RLO to the BR bit. |
| .... | // Any program |
| AN OV | // Query OV bit at end of block. |
| SAVE | // If there is an overflow, set BR bit to "0".  // Set BR to "1" if there is no overflow. |
| JBI END | // If BR = "1", jump to jump label END.  // If BR = "0", execute the next instruction. |
| R "Tag_Output_1" | // Reset operand "Tag_Output_1" to "0". |
| END: S "Tag_Output_2" | // Set operand "Tag_Output_2" to "1" |

---

[Setting status bits (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-s7-300-s7-400)

##### JNBI: Jump if BR = 0 (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Jump if BR = 0" instruction to interrupt the linear program execution depending on the binary result (BR) and resume it at the point marked by the specified jump label.

The jump to the specified jump label is only executed if the status bit BR is "0". If the status bit BR before the instruction is "1", the jump is not executed and the program resumes with the next instruction.

The "Jump if BR = 0" instruction sets the status bit STA to "1" and the status bits OR and /FC to "0" both when the condition is met and when it is not met.

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Jump if BR = 0" instruction:

| Parameters | Description |
| --- | --- |
| &lt;jump label&gt; | Symbolic name of the jump destination |

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| SET | // Set RLO at the start of block to "1" |
| SAVE | // Transfer signal state of the RLO to the BR bit. |
| .... | // Any program |
| AN OV | // Query OV bit at end of block. |
| SAVE | // If there is an overflow, set BR bit to "0".  // Set BR to "1" if there is no overflow. |
| JNBI END | // If BR = "0", jump to jump label END.  // If BR = "1", execute the next instruction. |
| S "Tag_Output" | // Set operand "Tag_Output" to "1" |
| END: BE | // End block |

---

**See also**

[Basic information on the status word (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#basic-information-on-the-status-word-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[Setting status bits in program control operation instructions (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-in-program-control-operation-instructions-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[Querying status bits with jump instructions (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#querying-status-bits-with-jump-instructions-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[Inserting STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#inserting-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[Setting status bits (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-s7-300-s7-400)

##### JO: Jump if OV = 1 (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Jump if OV = 1" instruction to interrupt linear program execution depending on the status bit OV and resume it at the point marked by the specified jump label.

The jump to the specified jump label is only executed if the status bit OV is "1". The status bit OV is set if, for example, the result of a calculation is outside the permitted range or an invalid value is returned during the comparison of floating-point numbers.

If the status bit OV is "0", the jump is not executed and the program continues with the next instruction.

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Jump if OV = 1" instruction:

| Parameters | Description |
| --- | --- |
| &lt;jump label&gt; | Symbolic name of the jump destination |

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Load value |
| *I | // Multiply values |
| JO OVER | // If the status bit OV has signal state "1", jump to jump label "OVER" and continue program execution there.  // If the signal state of the status bit OV is "0", execute the next instruction. |
| T "Tag_Result" | // Transfer the result of the multiplication to the operand "Tag_Result". |
| JU NEXT | // Jump to jump label "NEXT" and resume execution of the program there. |
| OVER: SET | // Continue program execution at this point if the condition (OV = "1") is satisfied.  // Set RLO to signal state "1" |
| R "Tag_Output" | // Reset operand "Tag_Output" to "0". |
| NEXT: A "MyTag_1" | // Jump label "NEXT"  // Query whether the value of operand "MyTag_1" is "1" and AND. |
| A "MyTag_2" | // Query whether the value of operand "MyTag_2" is "1" and AND. |
| S "Tag_Output_2" | // If RLO = 1, set the "Tag_Output_2" operand to "1". |

---

**See also**

[Basic information on the status word (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#basic-information-on-the-status-word-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[Setting status bits in program control operation instructions (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-in-program-control-operation-instructions-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[Querying status bits with jump instructions (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#querying-status-bits-with-jump-instructions-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[Inserting STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#inserting-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[Setting status bits (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-s7-300-s7-400)

##### JOS: Jump if OS = 1 (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Jump if OS = 1" instruction to interrupt linear program execution depending on the status bit OS and resume it at the point marked by the specified jump label.

The jump to the specified jump label is only executed if the status bit OS is "1". The status bit OS is always set when a number range overflow sets the status bit OV to "1". In contrast to status bit OV, the status bit OS remains set even if a result is subsequently in the permitted number range.

If the status bit OS is "0", the jump is not executed and the program continues with the next instruction.

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Jump if OS = 1" instruction:

| Parameters | Description |
| --- | --- |
| &lt;jump label&gt; | Symbolic name of the jump destination |

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Load value |
| *I | // Multiply loaded values.  // Store product in accumulator 1. |
| L "Tag_Value_3" | // Load value |
| +I | // Add loaded value to the product.  // Store product in accumulator 1. |
| L "Tag_Value_4" | // Load value |
| -I | // Subtract loaded value from the calculated sum.  // Store product in accumulator 1. |
| JOS OVER | // If there is an overflow in one of the three preceding instructions, the status bit OS is set to "1"  // If the signal state of the status bit OS is "1", the program resumes at the jump label "OVER".  // If the signal state of the status bit OS is "0", the next instruction is executed |
| T "Tag_Result" | // Transfer the result of the entire calculation to the operand "Tag_Result" |
| JU NEXT | // Jump to jump label "NEXT" and resume execution of the program there. |
| OVER: SET | // Continue program execution at this point if the condition (OV = "1") is satisfied.  // Set RLO to signal state "1" |
| R "Tag_Output" | // Reset operand "Tag_Output" to "0". |
| NEXT: A "MyTag_1" | // Jump label "NEXT"   // Query whether the value of operand "MyTag_1" is "1" and AND. |
| A "MyTag_2" | // Query whether the value of operand "MyTag_2" is "1" and AND. |
| S "Tag_Output_2" | // If RLO = 1, set the "Tag_Output_2" operand to "1". |

---

**See also**

[Basic information on the status word (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#basic-information-on-the-status-word-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[Setting status bits in program control operation instructions (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-in-program-control-operation-instructions-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[Querying status bits with jump instructions (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#querying-status-bits-with-jump-instructions-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[Inserting STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#inserting-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[Setting status bits (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-s7-300-s7-400)

##### JZ: Jump if the result is zero (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Jump if the result is zero" instruction to interrupt linear program execution depending on the status bits CC 0 and CC 1 and continue at the point marked by the specified jump label.

The jump to the specified jump label is only executed if the signal state of the status bits CC 0 and CC 1 is "0". The situation occurs when one of the following conditions applies:

- After processing an arithmetic instruction without overflow, accumulator 1 has the value "0".
- A negative overflow occurs when executing the "Add integers (16 bit)" (+I) or "Add double integers (32 bit)" (+D) instruction.
- The value gradually drops below the permitted range when processing an arithmetic instruction (floating-point arithmetic) with overflow.
- The content of accumulator 2 is equal to the content of accumulator 1 after the execution of a comparison instruction.
- The content of accumulator 1 is zero after the execution of a word logic operation.
- The value of the last shifted out bit is "0" after the execution of a shift instruction.

In all other cases the jump is not executed and the processing of the program is resumed with the next instruction.

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Jump if the result is zero" instruction:

| Parameters | Description |
| --- | --- |
| &lt;jump label&gt; | Symbolic name of the jump destination |

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value" | // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value". |
| SRW 1 | // Shift the contents of the right word in accumulator 1 one place to the right. |
| JZ ZERO | // If the signal state of the last bit shifted is "0", jump to jump label "OVER" and continue with program processing from there  // If the signal state of the last bit shifted is "1", execute the next instruction. |
| L "MyTag_1" | // Load value of the operand "MyTag_1" in accumulator 1 |
| INC 1 | // Add right-hand byte of accumulator 1 with the value "1". |
| T "Tag_Result_1" | // Transfer the result to operand "Tag_Result_1". |
| JU NEXT | // Jump to jump label "NEXT" and resume execution of the program there. |
| ZERO: L "MyTag_2" | // Jump label "ZERO"  // Load value of the operand "MyTag_2" in accumulator 1 |
| INC 1 | // Add right-hand byte of accumulator 1 with the value "1". |
| T "Tag_Result_2" | // Transfer the result to operand "Tag_Result_2". |
| NEXT: A "MyTag_3" | // Jump label "NEXT"  // Query whether the value of operand "MyTag_3" is "1" and AND. |
| A "MyTag_4" | // Query whether the value of operand "MyTag_4" is "1" and AND. |

---

**See also**

[Basic information on the status word (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#basic-information-on-the-status-word-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[Setting status bits in program control operation instructions (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-in-program-control-operation-instructions-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[Querying status bits with jump instructions (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#querying-status-bits-with-jump-instructions-s7-300-s7-400)

[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[Setting status bits (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-s7-300-s7-400)

##### JN: Jump if the result is not zero (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Jump if the result is not zero" instruction to interrupt linear program execution depending on the status bits CC 0 and CC 1 and continue at the point marked by the specified jump label.

The jump to the specified jump label is only executed if the signal states of the status bits CC 0 and CC 1 are different. The situation occurs when one of the following conditions applies:

- After processing an arithmetic instruction without overflow, the value of accumulator 1 is not equal to zero.
- A negative overflow occurs when processing an arithmetic instruction with integers (+I, -I, *I, +D, -D, *D).
- A positive overflow occurs when executing a math instruction with integers (+I, -I, *I, /I, +D, -D, *D, /D, NEGI, NEGD).
- A positive or negative overflow occurs when processing an arithmetic instruction with floating-point numbers.
- The content of accumulator 2 is not equal to the content of accumulator 1 after the execution of a comparison instruction.
- The content of accumulator 1 is not zero after the execution of a word logic operation.
- The value of the last shifted out bit is "1" after the execution of a shift instruction.

In all other cases the jump is not executed and the processing of the program is resumed with the next instruction.

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Jump if the result is not zero" instruction:

| Parameters | Description |
| --- | --- |
| &lt;jump label&gt; | Symbolic name of the jump destination |

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value of the operand "Tag_Valu_1". |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_2". |
| XOW | // Apply EXCLUSIVE OR logic operation |
| JN NOZERO | // If the value in accumulator 1 is not equal to zero, the jump to the "NOZERO" jump label is performed and program processing continues from there.  // If the value in accumulator 1 is equal to zero, the next instruction will be processed. |
| AN "MyTag_1" | // Query whether the value of operand "MyTag_1" is "0" and AND. |
| S "Tag_Output_1" | // If RLO is "1", set the operand "Tag_Output_1" to "1". |
| JU NEXT | // Jump to jump label "NEXT" and resume execution of the program there. |
| NOZERO: AN "MyTag_2" | // Jump label "NOZERO"  // Query whether the value of operand "MyTag_2" is "0" and AND. |
| S "Tag_Output_2" | // If RLO is "1", set the operand "Tag_Output_2" to "1" |
| NEXT: A "MyTag_3" | // Jump label "NEXT"  // Query whether the value of operand "MyTag_3" is "1" and AND. |
| A "MyTag_4" | // Query whether the value of operand "MyTag_4" is "1" and AND. |

---

**See also**

[Basic information on the status word (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#basic-information-on-the-status-word-s7-300-s7-400)

[Setting status bits (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-s7-300-s7-400)

##### JP: Jump if the result is greater than zero (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Jump if the result is greater than zero" instruction to interrupt linear program execution depending on the status bits CC 0 and CC 1 and continue at the point marked by the specified jump label.

The jump to the specified jump label is executed only if the signal state of status bit CC 0 is "0" and CC 1 is "1". The situation occurs when one of the following conditions applies:

- After processing an arithmetic instruction without overflow, the value of accumulator 1 is greater than zero.
- A negative overflow occurs when processing an arithmetic instruction with integers (+I, -I, *I, +D, -D, *D).
- A positive overflow occurs when processing an arithmetic instruction with integers (*I, /I, *D, /D).
- A positive overflow occurs when processing an arithmetic instruction with floating-point numbers.
- After the execution of a comparison instruction, the content of accumulator 2 is greater than the content of accumulator 1.
- The contents of accumulator 1 are not zero after the execution of a word logic operation.
- The value of the last shifted out bit is "1" after the execution of a shift instruction.

In all other cases the jump is not executed and the processing of the program is resumed with the next instruction.

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Jump if the result is greater than zero" instruction:

| Parameters | Description |
| --- | --- |
| &lt;jump label&gt; | Symbolic name of the jump destination |

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_1". |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_2". |
| -I | // Subtract value of the operand "Tag_Value_2" from the value of the operand "Tag_Value_1". |
| JP POSITIVE | // At a positive result value in accumulator "1" jump to jump label "POSITIVE" and continue program processing from there  // If the result in accumulator 1 is negative, execute the next instruction. |
| AN "MyTag_1" | // Query whether the value of operand "MyTag_1" is "0" and AND. |
| S "Tag_Output_1" | // If RLO is "1", set the operand "Tag_Output_1" to "1". |
| JU NEXT | // Jump to jump label "NEXT" and resume execution of the program there. |
| POSITIVE: AN "MyTag_2" | // Jump label "POSITIVE"  // Query whether the value of operand "MyTag_2" is "0" and AND. |
| S "Tag_Output_2" | // If RLO is "1", set the operand "Tag_Output_2" to "1". |
| NEXT: A "MyTag_3" | // Jump label "NEXT"  // Query whether the value of operand "MyTag_3" is "1" and AND. |
| A "MyTag_4" | // Query whether the value of operand "MyTag_4" is "1" and AND. |

---

**See also**

[Basic information on the status word (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#basic-information-on-the-status-word-s7-300-s7-400)

##### JM: Jump if the result is less than zero (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Jump if the result is less than zero" instruction to interrupt linear program execution depending on the status bits CC 0 and CC 1 and continue at the point marked by the specified jump label.

The jump to the specified jump label is executed only if the signal state of status bit CC 0 is "1" and CC 1 is "0". The situation occurs when one of the following conditions applies:

- After processing an arithmetic instruction without overflow, the value of accumulator 1 is less than zero.
- A negative overflow occurs when processing an arithmetic instruction with integers (*I, *D).
- A positive overflow occurs when processing an arithmetic instruction with integers (+I, -I, +D, -D, NEGI, NEGD).
- A negative overflow occurs when processing an arithmetic instruction with floating-point numbers.
- After the execution of a comparison instruction, the content of accumulator 2 is less than the content of accumulator 1.

In all other cases the jump is not executed and the processing of the program is resumed with the next instruction.

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Jump if the result is less than zero" instruction:

| Parameters | Description |
| --- | --- |
| &lt;jump label&gt; | Symbolic name of the jump destination |

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_1". |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_2". |
| -I | // Subtract value of the operand "Tag_Value_2" from the value of the operand "Tag_Value_1". |
| JM NEGATIVE | // At a negative result value in accumulator "1" jump to jump label "NEGATIVE" and continue program processing from there  // If the result in accumulator 1 is positive, execute the next instruction. |
| AN "MyTag_1" | // Query whether the value of operand "MyTag_1" is "0" and AND. |
| S "Tag_Output_1" | // If RLO is "1", set the operand "Tag_Output_1" to "1". |
| JU NEXT | // Jump to jump label "NEXT" and resume execution of the program there. |
| NEGATIVE: AN "MyTag_2" | // Jump label "NEGATIVE"  // Query whether the value of operand "MyTag_2" is "0" and AND. |
| S "Tag_Output_2" | // If RLO is "1", set the operand "Tag_Output_2" to "1". |
| NEXT: A "MyTag_3" | // Jump label "NEXT"  // Query whether the value of operand "MyTag_3" is "1" and AND. |
| A "MyTag_4" | // Query whether the value of operand "MyTag_4" is "1" and AND. |

##### JPZ: Jump if the result is greater than or equal to zero (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Jump if the result is greater than or equal to zero" instruction to interrupt linear program execution depending on the status bit CC 0 and continue it at the point marked by the specified jump label.

The jump to the specified jump label is only executed if the signal state of the status bit CC 0 is "0". The situation occurs when one of the following conditions applies:

- After processing an arithmetic instruction without overflow, the value of accumulator 1 is greater than or equal to zero.
- A negative overflow occurs when processing an arithmetic instruction with integers (+I, -I, *I, +D, -D, *D).
- A positive overflow occurs when processing an arithmetic instruction with integers (*I, /I, *D, /D).
- A positive overflow occurs when processing an arithmetic instruction with floating-point numbers.
- The value gradually drops below the permitted range when processing an arithmetic instruction (floating-point arithmetic) with overflow.
- After the execution of a comparison instruction, the content of accumulator 2 is greater than or equal to the content of accumulator 1.
- An instruction for word logic operation was executed.
- A shift instruction was executed.

In all other cases the jump is not executed and the processing of the program is resumed with the next instruction.

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Jump if the result is greater than or equal to zero" instruction:

| Parameters | Description |
| --- | --- |
| &lt;jump label&gt; | Symbolic name of the jump destination |

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_1". |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_2". |
| -I | // Subtract value of the operand "Tag_Value_2" from the value of the operand "Tag_Value_1". |
| JPZ REGULAR | // At a positive result value or null in accumulator "1" jump to jump label "REGULAR" and continue program processing from there  // If the result in accumulator 1 is negative, execute the next instruction. |
| AN "MyTag_1" | // Query whether the value of operand "MyTag_1" is "0" and AND. |
| S "Tag_Output_1" | // If RLO is "1", set the operand "Tag_Output_1" to "1". |
| JU NEXT | // Jump to jump label "NEXT" and resume execution of the program there. |
| REGULAR: AN "MyTag_2" | // Jump label "REGULAR"  // Query whether the value of operand "MyTag_2" is "0" and AND. |
| S "Tag_Output_2" | // If RLO is "1", set the operand "Tag_Output_2" to "1". |
| NEXT: A "MyTag_3" | // Jump label "NEXT"  // Query whether the value of operand "MyTag_3" is "1" and AND. |
| A "MyTag_4" | // Query whether the value of operand "MyTag_4" is "1" and AND. |

---

**See also**

[Basic information on the status word (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#basic-information-on-the-status-word-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[Setting status bits in program control operation instructions (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-in-program-control-operation-instructions-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[Querying status bits with jump instructions (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#querying-status-bits-with-jump-instructions-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[Inserting STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#inserting-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[Setting status bits (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-s7-300-s7-400)

##### JMZ: Jump if the result is less than or equal to zero (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Jump if the result is less than or equal to zero" instruction to interrupt linear program execution depending on the status bit CC 1 and continue it at the point marked by the specified jump label.

The jump to the specified jump label is only executed if the signal state of the status bit CC 1 is "0". The situation occurs when one of the following conditions applies:

- After processing an arithmetic instruction without overflow, the value of accumulator 1 is less than or equal to zero.
- A negative overflow occurs when processing an arithmetic instruction with integers (+I, *I, +D, *D).
- A positive overflow occurs when processing an arithmetic instruction with integers (+I, -I, +D, -D, NEGI, NEGD).
- A negative overflow occurs when processing an arithmetic instruction with floating-point numbers.
- The value gradually drops below the permitted range when processing an arithmetic instruction (floating-point arithmetic) with overflow.
- After the execution of a comparison instruction, the content of accumulator 2 is less than or equal to the content of accumulator 1.
- The value of accumulator 1 is equal to zero after processing a word logic.
- The value of the last shifted bit is equal to zero after processing a write instruction.

In all other cases the jump is not executed and the processing of the program is resumed with the next instruction.

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Jump if the result is less than or equal to zero" instruction:

| Parameters | Description |
| --- | --- |
| &lt;jump label&gt; | Symbolic name of the jump destination |

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_1". |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_2". |
| -I | // Subtract value of the operand "Tag_Value_2" from the value of the operand "Tag_Value_1". |
| JMZ MyLABEL | // At a negative result value or null in accumulator "1" jump to jump label "MyLABEL" and continue program processing from there  // If the result in accumulator 1 is positive, execute the next instruction. |
| AN "MyTag_1" | // Query whether the value of operand "MyTag_1" is "0" and AND. |
| S "Tag_Output_1" | // If RLO = "1", set the operand "Tag_Output_1" to "1" |
| JU NEXT | // Jump to jump label "NEXT" and resume execution of the program there. |
| MyLABEL: AN "MyTag_2" | // Jump label "MyLABEL"  // Query whether the value of operand "MyTag_2" is "0" and AND. |
| S "Tag_Output_2" | // If RLO="1" set the operand "Tag_Output_2" to "1" |
| NEXT: A "MyTag_3" | // Jump label "NEXT"  // Query whether the value of operand "MyTag_3" is "1" and AND. |
| A "MyTag_4" | // Query whether the value of operand "MyTag_4" is "1" and AND. |

---

**See also**

[Basic information on the status word (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#basic-information-on-the-status-word-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[Setting status bits in program control operation instructions (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-in-program-control-operation-instructions-s7-300-s7-400)

[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[Setting status bits (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-s7-300-s7-400)

##### JUO: Jump if the result is invalid (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Jump if the result is invalid" instruction to interrupt linear program execution depending on the status bits CC 0 and CC 1 and continue at the point marked by the specified jump label.

The jump to the specified jump label is only executed if the signal state of the status bits CC 0 and CC 1 is "1". The situation occurs when one of the following conditions applies:

- It is divided by zero with a mathematical instruction (/I, /D, MOD).
- When processing an arithmetic instruction with floating-point numbers an overflow occurs and the result value is an invalid floating-point number.
- When processing a comparative instruction with floating-point numbers an invalid floating-point number was used or occurred as a result value.

In all other cases the jump is not executed and the processing of the program is resumed with the next instruction.

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Jump if the result is invalid" instruction:

| Parameters | Description |
| --- | --- |
| &lt;jump label&gt; | Symbolic name of the jump destination |

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_1". |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_2". |
| /I | // Divide value of the operand "Tag_Value_1" by value of the operand "Tag_Value_2". |
| JUO ERROR | // At a division by zero, jump to jump label "ERROR" and continue with program processing from there  // Otherwise execute next instruction. |
| T "Tag_Result" | // Transfer contents of accumulator 1 to the operand "Tag_Result". |
| A "MyTag_1" | // Query whether the value of operand "MyTag_1" is "1" and AND. |
| R "MyTag_1" | // If RLO = "1", reset the operand "MyTag_1" to "0" |
| JU NEXT | // Jump to jump label "NEXT" and resume execution of the program there. |
| ERROR: AN "MyTag_1" | // Jump label "ERROR"  // Query whether the value of operand "MyTag_1" is "0" and AND. |
| S "MyTag_1" | // If RLO is "1", set the operand "MyTag_1" to "1". |
| NEXT: A "MyTag_3" | // Jump label "NEXT"  // Query whether the value of operand "MyTag_3" is "1" and AND. |
| A "MyTag_4" | // Query whether the value of operand "MyTag_4" is "1" and AND. |

---

**See also**

[Basic information on the status word (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#basic-information-on-the-status-word-s7-300-s7-400)

[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[Setting status bits (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-s7-300-s7-400)

##### JL: Define jump list (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the instruction "Define jump list" to program a list that consists of several entries of the instruction "Unconditional jump" (JU). The list begins directly after the instruction "Define jump list" and may contain up to 255 entries. The numbering of the jump functions in the list begins at zero. The jump list must be programmed without any gaps. The end of the jump list is marked by a jump label that is specified for the "Define jump list" instruction.

Which jump function of the list executes, depends on the value in the right byte of accumulator 1. If, for example, the accumulator 1 has the value "0", the first jump function executes. If the value in accumulator 1 is "1", the second jump function executes. If the value in accumulator 1 is greater than the number of list entries, the "Define jump list" instruction references the end of the list.

The "Jump distributor" instruction is processed independently of conditions and does not affect the status bits.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value" | // Load jump number in accumulator 1. |
| JL END | // Start of the jump list |
| JU MyLABEL_1 | // If the value is "0", execute in accumulator 1 and jump to jump label "MyLABEL_1" |
| JU MyLABEL_2 | // If the value is "1", execute in accumulator 1 and jump to jump label "MyLABEL_2" |
| JU MyLABEL_3 | // If the value is "2", execute in accumulator 1 and jump to jump label "MyLABEL_3" |
| END: L "MyTag_1" | // End of the jump list  // Load content of the operand "MyTag_1" in accumulator 1. |
| L "MyTag_2" | // Load content of the operand "MyTag_2" in accumulator 1. |
| +I | // Add values |
| T "Tag_Output_2" | // Load contents of accumulator 1 in operand "Tag_Output_2". |
| MyLABEL_1: ... | // Jump label "MyLABEL_1" |
| .... | // Any program |
| JU NEXT | // Jump to jump label "NEXT" and resume execution of the program there. |
| MyLABEL_2: ... | // Jump label "MyLABEL_2" |
| .... | // Any program |
| JU NEXT | // Jump to jump label "NEXT" and resume execution of the program there. |
| MyLABEL_3: ... | // Jump label "MyLABEL_3" |
| .... | // Any program |
| JU NEXT | // Jump to jump label "NEXT" and resume execution of the program there. |
| NEXT: ... | // Jump label "NEXT" |

---

**See also**

[Setting status bits in program control operation instructions (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-in-program-control-operation-instructions-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[Querying status bits with jump instructions (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#querying-status-bits-with-jump-instructions-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[Basic information on the status word (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#basic-information-on-the-status-word-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[Inserting STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#inserting-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[STL programming examples (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#stl-programming-examples-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

##### LOOP: Loop (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Loop" instruction to program loops in the program.

The instruction interprets the right word of accumulator 1 as an unsigned 16-bit integer in the range from 0 to 65535. During execution the instruction first decrements the content of accumulator 1 by one. If the value in accumulator 1 after the decrement is not zero, the jump is executed at the specified jump label. If the value is zero, the jump is not executed and the processing of the program is resumed with the next instruction. The value in accumulator 1 therefore specifies the number of program loops that have to be executed. This number has to be saved in a loop counter.

The operand &lt;number&gt; contains the number of the loop cycles. The operand &lt;Loop counter&gt; contains the number of the loop cycles still to be executed. At the end of the program loop, the content of the loop counter is loaded in accumulator 1 and decremented by one by the instruction. The jump to the jump label at the start of the program loop is executed if the value in the accumulator is not equal to zero after the decrement.

The "Loop" instruction does not affect any status bits.

> **Note**
>
> If the loop counter is not preset or is preset with the value "0", the loop counter is decremented further and further into the negative, resulting in an endless loop that can change the CPU to STOP mode.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value" | // Load number of time loop will execute into the right word of accumulator 1. |
| START: T "Tag_Counter" | // Start of the jump list  // Transfer contents of accumulator 1 to the loop counter. |
| L "MyTag_1" | // Load value of the operand "MyTag_1". |
| L "MyTag_2" | // Load value of the operand "MyTag_2". |
| *D | // Multiply values |
| T "MyTag_1" | // Transfer the result of the multiplication to the operand "MyTag_1". |
| L "Tag_Counter" | // Load value of the loop counter into accumulator 1. |
| LOOP START | // Decrement value in accumulator 1 by one.  // Jump to the start of the program loop if the value is not equal to zero.  // If the value is zero, execute the next instruction. |
| L "MyTag_2" | // Load value of the operand "MyTag_2". |
| L 100 | // Load the value 100. |
| &gt;I | // Compare whether the value of the operand "MyTag_2" is greater than 200. |
| = "MyTag_3" | // Write comparison result to the operand "MyTag_3". |

---

**See also**

[Setting status bits in program control operation instructions (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-in-program-control-operation-instructions-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[Querying status bits with jump instructions (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#querying-status-bits-with-jump-instructions-s7-300-s7-400)

#### Data blocks (S7-300, S7-400)

This section contains information on the following topics:

- [OPN: Open global data block (S7-300, S7-400)](#opn-open-global-data-block-s7-300-s7-400)
- [OPNDI: Open instance data block (S7-300, S7-400)](#opndi-open-instance-data-block-s7-300-s7-400)
- [CDB: Swap data block register (S7-300, S7-400)](#cdb-swap-data-block-register-s7-300-s7-400)
- [L DBLG: Load the length of a global data block into accumulator 1 (S7-300, S7-400)](#l-dblg-load-the-length-of-a-global-data-block-into-accumulator-1-s7-300-s7-400)
- [L DBNO: Load the number of a global data block into accumulator 1 (S7-300, S7-400)](#l-dbno-load-the-number-of-a-global-data-block-into-accumulator-1-s7-300-s7-400)
- [L DILG: Load the length of an instance data block into accumulator 1 (S7-300, S7-400)](#l-dilg-load-the-length-of-an-instance-data-block-into-accumulator-1-s7-300-s7-400)
- [L DINO: Load the number of an instance data block into accumulator 1 (S7-300, S7-400)](#l-dino-load-the-number-of-an-instance-data-block-into-accumulator-1-s7-300-s7-400)

##### OPN: Open global data block (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

You can open a global data block (DB) with the "Open global data block" instruction. The number of the data block is transferred to the DB register. Subsequent DB commands access the relevant blocks depending on the content of the register.

The "Open global data block" instruction is processed without any conditions and does not affect either the result of logic operation or the accumulator contents.

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Open global data block" instruction:

| Operand | Declaration | Data block type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;data block&gt; | - | DB | Data block that will be opened. |

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| OPN "GlobalDataBlock" | // Open global data block. |
| L %DBW0 | // Load data word DBW0 of the opened global data block into accumulator 1. |
| T "MyTag" | // Transfer contents of accumulator 1 to the operand "MyTag_1". |

---

**See also**

[Setting status bits in program control operation instructions (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-in-program-control-operation-instructions-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[Basic information on the status word (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#basic-information-on-the-status-word-s7-300-s7-400)
