#### Accumulators (S7-300, S7-400)

This section contains information on the following topics:

- [TAK: Swap content of accumulators 1 and 2 (S7-300, S7-400)](#tak-swap-content-of-accumulators-1-and-2-s7-300-s7-400)
- [PUSH: Shift content to the next higher accumulator (S7-300, S7-400)](#push-shift-content-to-the-next-higher-accumulator-s7-300-s7-400)
- [POP: Shift content to the next lower accumulator (S7-300, S7-400)](#pop-shift-content-to-the-next-lower-accumulator-s7-300-s7-400)
- [ENT: Shift accumulators 2 and 3 to the next higher accumulator (S7-300, S7-400)](#ent-shift-accumulators-2-and-3-to-the-next-higher-accumulator-s7-300-s7-400)
- [LEAVE: Shift accumulators 3 and 4 to the next lower accumulator (S7-300, S7-400)](#leave-shift-accumulators-3-and-4-to-the-next-lower-accumulator-s7-300-s7-400)

##### TAK: Swap content of accumulators 1 and 2 (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the instruction "Swap content of accumulators 1 and 2" to switch the contents accumulator 1 with the contents of accumulator 2. In case of controllers with four accumulators, the contents of accumulators 3 and 4 are not influenced by the instruction.

The CPU executes the instruction regardless of the result of logic operation and the status bit. The instruction does not affect either the result of logic operation or the status bit.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_1" in accumulator 1. |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Shift the contents of accumulator 1 to accumulator 2.  // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_2" in accumulator 1 |
| &gt;I | // Compare whether the value of accumulator 2 is greater than the value of accumulator 1. |
| JC NEXT | // If condition is satisfied (RLO = "1"), jump to jump label NEXT.  // If the condition is not satisfied (RLO = "0"), execute the next instruction. |
| TAK | // Swap the contents of accumulators 1 and 2. |
| NEXT: -I | // Jump label "NEXT"  // Subtract value of accumulator 1 from value of accumulator 2. |
| T "Tag_Output" | // Transfer contents of accumulator 1 to the operand "Tag_Output". |

---

**See also**

[Inserting STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#inserting-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

##### PUSH: Shift content to the next higher accumulator (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Shift content to the next higher accumulator" instruction to move the contents of the accumulators 1 to 3 to the next higher accumulator.

In case of controllers with 2 accumulators, only the contents of accumulator 1 are copied to accumulator 2.

In controls with 4 accumulators, the content of accumulator 1 is moved to accumulator 2; the content of accumulator 2 is moved to accumulator 3 and the content of accumulator 3 to accumulator 4. The content of accumulator 4 will be lost.

The content of accumulator 1 is not influenced by the instruction and remains unchanged after processing the instruction.

The following table shows the contents of accumulators 1 to 4 before and after the processing of the instruction:

| Status | Accumulator |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| 1 | 2 | 3 | 4 |  |
| Before processing | Value A | Value B | Value C | Value D |
| After processing | Value A | Value A | Value B | Value C |

The CPU executes the instruction regardless of the result of logic operation and the status bit. The instruction does not affect either the result of logic operation or the status bit.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value of the operand in accumulator 1. |
| PUSH | // Shift contents of accumulators 1 to 3 to the next higher accumulator. |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Load value of the operand in accumulator 1. |

---

**See also**

[Inserting STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#inserting-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

##### POP: Shift content to the next lower accumulator (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Shift content to the next lower accumulator" instruction to move the contents of the accumulators 4 to 2 to the next lower accumulator.

In controls with 2 accumulators the content of accumulator 2 will be moved to accumulator 1.

In controls with 4 accumulators, the content of accumulator 4 is moved to accumulator 3; the content of accumulator 3 is moved to accumulator 2 and the content of accumulator 2 to accumulator 1. The content of accumulator 1 will be lost.

The content of accumulator 4 is not influenced by the instruction and remains unchanged after processing the instruction.

The following table shows the contents of accumulators 1 to 4 before and after the processing of the instruction:

| Status | Accumulator |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| 1 | 2 | 3 | 4 |  |
| Before processing | Value A | Value B | Value C | Value D |
| After processing | Value B | Value C | Value D | Value D |

The CPU executes the instruction regardless of the result of logic operation and the status bit. The instruction does not affect either the result of logic operation or the status bit.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| T "Tag_Value_1" | // Transfer contents of accumulator 1 to the operand "Tag_Value_1". |
| POP | // Shift content of accumulators 4 to 2 to the next lower accumulator |
| T "Tag_Value_2" | // Transfer contents of accumulator 1 to the operand "Tag_Value_2". |

---

**See also**

[Inserting STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#inserting-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

##### ENT: Shift accumulators 2 and 3 to the next higher accumulator (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

With the "Shift accumulators 2 and 3 to the next higher accumulator" you shift the contents of accumulator 3 to accumulator 4 and the contents of accumulator 2 to accumulator 3. The content of accumulators 1 and 2 remains unchanged.

The following table shows the contents of accumulators 1 to 4 before and after the processing of the instruction:

| Status | Accumulator |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| 1 | 2 | 3 | 4 |  |
| Before processing | Value A | Value B | Value C | Value D |
| After processing | Value A | Value B | Value B | Value C |

The CPU executes the instruction regardless of the result of logic operation and the status bit. The instruction does not affect either the result of logic operation or the status bit.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_1" in accumulator 1 |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Shift the contents of accumulator 1 to accumulator 2.  // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_2" in accumulator 1 |
| *R | // Multiply the values of accumulator 1 and 2.  // Store product (intermediate result) in accumulator 1. |
| L "Tag_Value_3" | // Shift the content of accumulator 1 (intermediate result) to accumulator 2.  // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_3" in accumulator 1 |
| ENT | // Copy the content of accumulator 2 (intermediate result) to accumulator 3.  // Copy the content of accumulator 3 to accumulator 4. |
| L "Tag_Value_4" | // Move the contents of accumulator 1 ("Tag_Value_3") to accumulator 2.  // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_4" in accumulator 1 |
| +R | // Add the values of accumulator 1 and 2.  // Store sum in accumulator 1.  // Transfer the value of accumulator 3 (intermediate result) to accumulator 2. |
| LEAVE | // Shift the content of accumulator 3 (intermediate result) to accumulator 2.  // Shift the contents of accumulator 4 to accumulator 3. |
| /R | // Divide the values of accumulator 1 and 2.  // Store result in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Result" | // Transfer result (contents of accumulator 1) to the operand "Tag_Result". |

---

**See also**

[Inserting STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#inserting-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

##### LEAVE: Shift accumulators 3 and 4 to the next lower accumulator (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

With the "Shift accumulators 3 and 4 to the next lower accumulator" you shift the content of accumulator 3 to accumulator 2 and the content of accumulator 4 to accumulator 3. The content of accumulators 1 and 4 remains unchanged.

Instructions for arithmetic calculations include the functionality of the "Shift accumulators 3 and 4 to the next lower accumulator" instruction.

The following table shows the contents of accumulators 1 to 4 before and after the processing of the instruction:

| Status | Accumulator |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| 1 | 2 | 3 | 4 |  |
| Before processing | Value A | Value B | Value C | Value D |
| After processing | Value A | Value C | Value D | Value D |

The CPU executes the instruction regardless of the result of logic operation and the status bit. The instruction does not affect either the result of logic operation or the status bit.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_1" in accumulator 1. |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Shift the contents of accumulator 1 to accumulator 2.  // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_2" in accumulator 1 |
| AD | // AND the value of accumulator 2 Tag_Value_1 with the value of accumulator 1 ("Tag_Value_2")  // Store result in accumulator 1. |
| L "Tag_Value_3" | // Shift the contents of accumulator 1 (intermediate result) to accumulator 2.  // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_3" in accumulator 1 |
| ENT | // Copy the content of accumulator 2 (intermediate result) to accumulator 3.  // Copy the content of accumulator 3 to accumulator 4. |
| L "Tag_Value_4" | // Move the contents of accumulator 1 ("Tag_Value_3") to accumulator 2.  // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_4" in accumulator 1 |
| AD | // AND the value of accumulator 2 Tag_Value_3 with the value of accumulator 1 ("Tag_Value_4")  // Store result in accumulator 1. |
| LEAVE | // Shift the contents of accumulator 3 (intermediate result) to accumulator 2.  // Shift the contents of accumulator 4 to accumulator 3. |
| OD | // OR the value of accumulator 2 with the value of accumulator 1  // Store result in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_Result" | // Transfer the result to operand "Tag_Result". |

---

**See also**

[Inserting STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#inserting-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

#### Address register (S7-300, S7-400)

This section contains information on the following topics:

- [+AR1: Add accumulator 1 to AR1 (S7-300, S7-400)](#ar1-add-accumulator-1-to-ar1-s7-300-s7-400)
- [+AR2: Add accumulator 1 to AR2 (S7-300, S7-400)](#ar2-add-accumulator-1-to-ar2-s7-300-s7-400)

##### +AR1: Add accumulator 1 to AR1 (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

With the "Add accumulator 1 to AR1" instruction you add a value to the content of address register 1. The type of pointer located in address register 1 and the operand range remain as they are.

The following options are available for specifying the value to be added:

- Specification via a constant: The instruction adds the value of the constant to address register 1. The value of the constant must correspond to the format of a range-internal pointer (POINTER).
- Specification via the value of the right word in the accumulator 1: The instruction interprets the value of the right word in accumulator 1 as a 16-bit integer and extends it with the correct sign to 24 bits. The instruction then adds value of accumulator 1 to address register 1. Values from -32768 to +32767 are permitted.

The CPU executes the instruction regardless of the result of logic operation and the status bit. The instruction does not affect either the result of logic operation or the status bit.

The contents of the accumulators are not changed by the instruction.

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Add accumulator 1 to AR1" instruction:

| Parameters | Data type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;constant&gt; | POINTER | Value that is added to address register 1. |

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| +AR1 P#10.0 | // Add pointer to address register 1. |
| L "Tag_Value" | // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value" into the right word of accumulator 1. |
| +AR1 | // Add value of accumulator 1 to address register 1. |
| TAR1 %MD24 | // Transfer contents of address register 1 to double word MD24. |

---

**See also**

[Inserting STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#inserting-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

##### +AR2: Add accumulator 1 to AR2 (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

With the "Add accumulator 1 to AR2" instruction you add a value to the content of address register 2. The type of pointer located in address register 2 and the operand range remain as they are.

The following options are available for specifying the value to be added:

- Specification via a constant: The instruction adds the value of the constant to address register 2. The value of the constant must correspond to the format of a range-internal pointer (POINTER).
- Specification via the value of the right word in the accumulator 1: The instruction interprets the value of the right word in accumulator 1 as a 16-bit integer and extends it with the correct sign to 24 bits. The instruction then adds value of accumulator 1 to address register 2. Values from -32768 to +32767 are permitted.

The CPU executes the instruction regardless of the result of logic operation and the status bit. The instruction does not affect either the result of logic operation or the status bit.

The contents of the accumulators are not changed by the instruction.

> **Note**
>
> Address register AR2 is used when processing multi-instances. If you program the "Add accumulator 1 to AR2" instruction, you must first "save" the contents of address register 2 and reload it later.

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Add accumulator 1 to AR2" instruction:

| Parameters | Data type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;constant&gt; | POINTER | Value that is added to address register 1. |

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| +AR2 P#10.0 | // Add pointer to address register 2. |
| L "Tag_Value" | // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value" into the right word of accumulator 1. |
| +AR2 | // Add value of accumulator 1 to address register 2. |
| TAR2 %MD24 | // Transfer contents of address register 1 to double word MD24. |

---

**See also**

[Inserting STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#inserting-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

#### Master Control Relay (S7-300, S7-400)

This section contains information on the following topics:

- [MCR(: Open MCR ranges (S7-300, S7-400)](#mcr-open-mcr-ranges-s7-300-s7-400)
- [)MCR: Close MCR ranges (S7-300, S7-400)](#mcr-close-mcr-ranges-s7-300-s7-400)
- [MCRA: Enable MCR range (S7-300, S7-400)](#mcra-enable-mcr-range-s7-300-s7-400)
- [MCRD: Disable MCR range (S7-300, S7-400)](#mcrd-disable-mcr-range-s7-300-s7-400)

##### MCR(: Open MCR ranges (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the "Open MCR ranges" instruction to switch the MCR dependency of an MCR range on and off depending on the result of logic operation (RLO).

Use the instructions "Enable MCR range" (MCRA) and "Disable MCR range" (MCRD) to specify the start and end of an MCR range. Within the defined MCR range you can switch the MCR dependency on and off for one or more program sections.

> **Note**
>
> Read the information in the section "Important notes on using the MCR functionality" in "See also".

The MCR dependency is switched on when the RLO is "1" before processing of the instruction. If the RLO is "0" before the instruction, the MCR dependency is switched off. The end of the MCR dependent program section is programmed using the instruction "Close MCR range". The program section between the two instructions is affected by the MCR. Only the MCR-dependent instructions (for example, the "Transfer" instruction (T)) are affected.

You can also nest the switching on and off of MCR dependency by programming the "Open MCR ranges" instruction in an MCR-dependent program section. You can nest the instruction up to 8 levels deep. The MCR dependency of the higher-level program section hereby controls the MCR dependencies in all lower-level program sections. If the MCR dependency is switched off in the higher-level program section, this MCR dependency cannot be switched on in any of the lower-level MCR dependent program sections.

If you call a block within an MCR range, the MCR dependency is disabled in the called block. When the block is exited, the MCR dependency is set so that it is the same as before the block call.

The instructions "Open MCR ranges" and "Close MCR ranges" must always be programmed in pairs. If one of the two instructions is not programmed, an MCR stack error is triggered.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| MCRA | // Start of the MCR range |
| A "Tag_Input_1" | // Query operand for "1" and link with the current RLO according to AND. |
| MCR( | // Start of the MCR dependency  // If signal state of RLO is "1", switch on MCR dependency.  // If signal state of RLO is "0", switch off MCR dependency. |
| A "Tag_Input_2" | // Query operand for "1" and link with the current RLO according to AND. |
| = "Tag_Output_1" | // If MCR dependency is switched off, reset operand to "0".  // If MCR dependency is switched on, set or reset operand depending on RLO |
| A "Tag_Input_3" | // Query operand for "1" and link with the current RLO according to AND. |
| MCR( | // Nesting of MCR dependency |
| A "Tag_Input_4" | // Query operand for "1" and link with the current RLO according to AND. |
| A "Tag_Input_5" | // Query operand for "1" and link with the current RLO according to AND. |
| = "Tag_Output_2" | // If MCR dependency is switched off, reset operand to "0".  // If MCR dependency is switched on, set or reset operand depending on RLO |
| )MCR | // End of the nesting |
| L "Tag_InputValue_1" | // Load value of the operand in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_OutputValue_1" | // If MCR dependency is switched off, write the value "0" to the operand.  // If MCR dependency is switched on, transfer the contents of accumulator 1 to the operand. |
| )MCR | // End of the MCR dependency |
| A "Tag_Input_6" | // Query operand for "1" and link with the current RLO according to AND. |
| MCR( | // Start of the MCR dependency  // If signal state of RLO is "1", switch on MCR dependency.  // If signal state of RLO is "0", switch off MCR dependency. |
| L "Tag_InputValue_2" | // Load value of the operand in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_OutputValue_2" | // If MCR dependency is switched off, write the value "0" to the operand.  // If MCR dependency is switched on, transfer the contents of accumulator 1 to the operand. |
| )MCR | // End of the MCR dependency |
| MCRD | // End of the MCR range |
| A "Tag_Input_7" | // Query operand for "1" and link with the current RLO according to AND. |
| = "Tag_Output_3" | // Set or reset operand depending on RLO |

---

**See also**

[Important notes on using MCR functions (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#important-notes-on-using-mcr-functions-s7-300-s7-400)

[Inserting STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#inserting-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

##### )MCR: Close MCR ranges (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

The "Close MCR ranges" instruction completes an MCR dependent program section. In this case the instruction deletes the RLO from the last entry in the MCR stack.

> **Note**
>
> Read the information in the section "Important notes on using the MCR functionality" in "See also".

Use the instruction "Open MCR ranges" to program the MCR dependency. The instructions "Open MCR ranges" and "Close MCR ranges" must always be programmed in pairs. If one of the two instructions is not programmed, an MCR stack error is triggered.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| MCRA | // Start of the MCR range |
| A "Tag_Input_1" | // Query operand for "1" and link with the current RLO according to AND. |
| MCR( | // Start of the MCR dependency  // If signal state of RLO is "1", switch on MCR dependency.  // If signal state of RLO is "0", switch off MCR dependency. |
| A "Tag_Input_2" | // Query operand for "1" and link with the current RLO according to AND. |
| = "Tag_Output_1" | // If MCR dependency is switched off, reset operand to "0".  // If MCR dependency is switched on, set or reset operand depending on RLO |
| L "Tag_InputValue" | // Load value of the operand in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_OutputValue" | // If MCR dependency is switched off, write the value "0" to the operand.  // If MCR dependency is switched on, transfer the contents of accumulator 1 to the operand. |
| )MCR | // End of the MCR dependency |
| MCRD | // End of the MCR range |
| A "Tag_Input_3" | // Query operand for "1" and link with the current RLO according to AND. |
| = "Tag_Output_2" | // Set or reset operand depending on RLO |

---

**See also**

[Important notes on using MCR functions (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#important-notes-on-using-mcr-functions-s7-300-s7-400)

[Inserting STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#inserting-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

##### MCRA: Enable MCR range (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the instruction "Enable MCR range" to specify the start of an MCR range. Within this range you can switch MCR dependency on and off using the following instructions:

- MCR(: Open MCR ranges
- )MCR: Close MCR ranges

You specify the end of the MCR range with the instruction "Disable MCR range" (MCRD). The instructions for defining the start and the end of an MCR range must always be used in pairs.

> **Note**
>
> Read the information in the section "Important notes on using the MCR functionality" in "See also".

If you call a block within an MCR range, the MCR dependency is disabled in the called block. When a block is exited, the MCR dependency is set so that it is the same as before the block call.

The instruction is executed regardless of the status bits and without affecting these bits.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| MCRA | // Start of the MCR range |
| A "Tag_Input_1" | // Query operand for "1" and link with the current RLO according to AND. |
| MCR( | // Start of the MCR dependency  // If signal state of RLO is "1", switch on MCR dependency.  // If signal state of RLO is "0", switch off MCR dependency. |
| A "Tag_Input_2" | // Query operand for "1" and link with the current RLO according to AND. |
| = "Tag_Output_1" | // If MCR dependency is switched off, reset operand to "0".  // If MCR dependency is switched on, set or reset operand depending on RLO |
| L "Tag_InputValue" | // Load value of the operand in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_OutputValue" | // If MCR dependency is switched off, write the value "0" to the operand.  // If MCR dependency is switched on, transfer the contents of accumulator 1 to the operand. |
| )MCR | // End of the MCR dependency |
| MCRD | // End of the MCR range |
| A "Tag_Input_3" | // Query operand for "1" and link with the current RLO according to AND. |
| = "Tag_Output_2" | // Set or reset operand depending on RLO |

---

**See also**

[Important notes on using MCR functions (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#important-notes-on-using-mcr-functions-s7-300-s7-400)

[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

##### MCRD: Disable MCR range (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

Use the instruction "Disable MCR range" to specify the end of an MCR range.

You specify the start of the MCR range with the instruction "Enable MCR range" (MCRA). The instructions for defining the start and the end of an MCR range must always be used in pairs.

> **Note**
>
> Read the information in the section "Important notes on using the MCR functionality" in "See also".

Within an MCR range you can program the MCR dependency with the help of the following instructions:

- MCR(: Open MCR ranges
- )MCR: Close MCR ranges

If you call a block within an MCR range, the MCR dependency is disabled in the called block. When a block is exited, the MCR dependency is set so that it is the same as before the block call.

The instruction is executed regardless of the status bits and without affecting these bits.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| MCRA | // Start of the MCR range |
| A "Tag_Input_1" | // Query operand for "1" and link with the current RLO according to AND. |
| MCR( | // Start of the MCR dependency  // If signal state of RLO is "1", switch on MCR dependency.  // If signal state of RLO is "0", switch off MCR dependency. |
| A "Tag_Input_2" | // Query operand for "1" and link with the current RLO according to AND. |
| = "Tag_Output_1" | // If MCR dependency is switched off, reset operand to "0".  // If MCR dependency is switched on, set or reset operand depending on RLO |
| L "Tag_InputValue" | // Load value of the operand in accumulator 1. |
| T "Tag_OutputValue" | // If MCR dependency is switched off, write the value "0" to the operand.  // If MCR dependency is switched on, transfer the contents of accumulator 1 to the operand. |
| )MCR | // End of the MCR dependency |
| MCRD | // End of the MCR range |
| A "Tag_Input_3" | // Query operand for "1" and link with the current RLO according to AND. |
| = "Tag_Output_2" | // Set or reset operand depending on RLO. |

---

**See also**

[Important notes on using MCR functions (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#important-notes-on-using-mcr-functions-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[Setting status bits in program control operation instructions (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-in-program-control-operation-instructions-s7-300-s7-400)

#### Null instructions (S7-300, S7-400)

This section contains information on the following topics:

- [BLD: Program display (null instruction) (S7-300, S7-400)](#bld-program-display-null-instruction-s7-300-s7-400)
- [NOP 0: Null instruction (S7-300, S7-400)](#nop-0-null-instruction-s7-300-s7-400)
- [NOP 1: Null instruction (S7-300, S7-400)](#nop-1-null-instruction-s7-300-s7-400)

##### BLD: Program display (null instruction) (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

The instruction "Program display (null instruction)" does not execute any function and does not affect the status bits. The instruction is used to recognize code sequences during a parameter transfer or with LAD/FBD networks. It is created automatically when a LAD or FBD program is displayed in STL. The parameter value is the number of the instruction and is generated by the programming device.

###### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Program display (null instruction)" instruction:

| Parameters | Data type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;number&gt; | WORD | Number of the instruction |

---

**See also**

[Inserting STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#inserting-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)
  
[Editing STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#editing-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

##### NOP 0: Null instruction (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

If "Null instruction" has a parameter 0, it does not execute any function and does not affect the status bits. The instruction code contains a bit pattern with 16 zeros. The instruction is only relevant for the programming device when a program is displayed.

###### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

| STL | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| L "Tag_Value_1" | // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_1" in accumulator 1. |
| L "Tag_Value_2" | // Shift the contents of accumulator 1 to accumulator 2.  // Load value of the operand "Tag_Value_2" in accumulator 1 |
| &gt;I | // Compare whether the value of accumulator 2 is greater than the value of accumulator 1. |
| A | // Query the signal state of the operand for "1" and AND with the current RLO. |
| JC NEXT | // If condition is satisfied (RLO = "1"), jump to jump label NEXT.  // If the condition is not satisfied (RLO = "0"), execute the next instruction. |
| TAK | // Swap the contents of accumulators 1 and 2. |
| NEXT: NOP 0 | // Jump label "NEXT" |

---

**See also**

[Inserting STL instructions (S7-300, S7-400, S7-1500)](Creating%20STL%20programs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%2C%20S7-1500%29.md#inserting-stl-instructions-s7-300-s7-400-s7-1500)

##### NOP 1: Null instruction (S7-300, S7-400)

###### Description

If "Null instruction" has a parameter 1, it does not execute any function and does not affect the status bits. The instruction code contains a bit pattern with 16 ones. The instruction is only relevant for the programming device when a program is displayed.
